Bulgaria, Diplomats Form New Cabinet, Strict Prevention of Riots in the Country 47

(Sofia) The King of Bulgaria has appointed former diplomat Toshev as Prime Minister. The King consulted with leaders of various political parties and key military personnel before issuing this appointment today. It is believed that the temporary implementation of military rule was discussed. This political crisis was triggered by the arrest of two former Prime Ministers and several famous politicians in the country. The release of these two is currently being considered, and strict precautions are being taken to prevent riots. (19th Reuters Dispatch)

(Sofia) The military cabinet members of the former cabinet held a long meeting today, and then went to see King Boris, but the King did not order them to form a cabinet, but instead appointed the famous political commentator Toshev, who had served in the diplomatic field, to try to form a new cabinet. It is generally believed that the King does not want the new cabinet to have a purely military cabinet form due to diplomatic relations. Generally speaking, the important cabinet members of the Toshev cabinet will be (1) Foreign Minister Koseivanov, (2) Finance Minister Ganazhinsky, (3) Justice Minister Digov, (4) Army Minister General Shiradov. Shiradov is the former Prime Minister of the former cabinet. Including him, there are three senior military officers in the new cabinet. As for Digov, he was originally the Minister of Justice of the former cabinet. The cabinet crisis was caused by his resignation and the resignation of two other cabinet members. (19th Havas Dispatch)

(Sofia) Although the famous political commentator Toshev has been ordered to form a cabinet, he has encountered some difficulties. The former Minister of Justice, Digov, requested that the former Prime Minister Zangov be released immediately as a condition for joining the cabinet. The former Prime Minister, General Shiradov, originally planned to be transferred to the position of Army Minister, but now he will not join the new cabinet. The position of Army Minister will therefore be taken by General Radev. However, after the formation of the new cabinet, regardless of the personnel, it will be approved by King Boris. It is generally believed that the choice of the new Prime Minister in this cabinet reshuffle is entirely from the will of the King and has not been subject to any restrictions, which is in line with the spirit of the constitution. Some quarters also believe that the new government is the first step towards restoring parliamentary politics. The military will definitely express its approval. (20th Havas Dispatch)

Japanese Iron and Steel Products Change from Net Imports to Net Exports, Result of the Development of the Military Industry 49

(Tokyo) Since the development of Japan's military industry, imports of iron and steel products, which were previously imported from abroad, have been greatly reduced. Japanese Air Force Establishes Three New Regiments, Concurrently Establishes Youth Aviation and Technical Schools 50

(Tokyo) The Army Ministry's four-year aviation plan, with an initial budget of over 48.3 million yuan, has passed the Diet and will be implemented separately from mid-April. The plans to be implemented this year are as follows:

(1) Establishment of new aviation schools: The Japanese Air Force has decided to increase three regiments, which requires a large number of aviation personnel. Therefore, the Army has decided to expand the Tokorozawa Aviation School to provide operational and academic training for aviation officers, as well as flight operation techniques for aviation non-commissioned officers and active-duty soldiers. In addition to expanding the existing aviation school, new Army Aviation Technical Schools and Army Youth Aviation Schools will be established. (2) Establishment of two new aviation regiments in Korea and Taiwan: The Japanese Army has decided to establish one new aviation regiment each in central Japan, northern Korea, and northern Taiwan, for a total of three new regiments. Surveying for the location of the new air bases has begun. (20th China United Press dispatch)

The Memel Issue 53

Lithuanian Capital Representatives from Great Britain, France, Japan, and Italy, the signatory countries of the Memel Convention, yesterday presented a formal protest to the Lithuanian government, urging it to respect the autonomous system of the Memel region. After the death sentence of members of the National Socialist Party in the region, each of the signatory countries had sent a note to the Lithuanian government last month, stating that the current administrative head of the Memel region had failed to gain the trust of the regional autonomous council, which violated the principles of the Memel autonomous system. They stated that the Lithuanian government should pay attention to this. Subsequently, Lithuania replied, attributing all responsibility to a certain country (referring to Germany), and stated that if the four countries of Great Britain, France, Japan, and Italy still insisted on their original viewpoint, they would submit the dispute to the Council of the League of Nations or the Permanent Court of International Justice in The Hague. (20th Havas dispatch)

Roosevelt Forms Cabinet Special Committee 57

(Washington) President Roosevelt today organized a special Cabinet committee, consisting of the Secretaries of Agriculture, Commerce, and Labor, to study the current status of the American cotton industry and the urgent issues concerning its future. President Roosevelt instructed the committee to investigate the following points: (1) The relationship between the processing tax and the current situation, and whether there are other methods of collecting this tax that are more efficient and less disruptive to the cotton industry. (2) Whether the collection of the processing tax has a detrimental impact on the cotton industry's situation in the near future. (3) The current price of raw cotton and its potential impact on consumption. President Roosevelt also instructed the committee to analyze the possibilities of foreign trade. (19th Reuters dispatch)

Reaction to Britain's Increased Import Duty on Soybeans 58

(London) After the 1935-36 budget increased the import duty on soybeans imported from the three northeastern provinces of China, the Financial News criticized it sharply, stating: "Soybeans have a wide range of uses, such as for making bread, refining artificial butter, making soy sauce, and feeding livestock. There are more than a hundred uses in total. Britain does not produce this item. Although there are some places engaged in planting, the quantity is extremely small unless the government subsidizes it. As for the various parts of the empire, they also do not produce this item. The large source of supply is from one corner of the three northeastern provinces. The only justifiable reason for the government's increase in import duty is that soybeans can compete with certain kinds of vegetable oils produced by the empire. It is known that the three northeastern provinces do not export much soybean oil and soybean cake. In short, the government's move is to exclude raw materials from other countries and encourage the other raw materials produced by the empire to replace them. This is something that Chancellor of the Exchequer Chamberlain cannot frankly admit." (20th Havas dispatch)

US House Passes Unemployment and Pension Bill 59

(Washington) The House of Representatives recently passed the unemployment and pension insurance bill proposed by the government by a vote of 372 to 33. This bill, in principle, allows each state to establish its own worker pension and unemployment insurance system under the supervision of the federal government. However, if the states are unable to establish a pension and insurance system, or if the funds allocated are insufficient for application, the central government will collect federal taxes to provide relief. In addition, this bill also permits the allocation of subsidies for various matters in each state, such as relief for children, mothers, illnesses, and work-related injuries. (19th Havas dispatch)

Military Personnel Scattered by the Enemy Who Return to Their Hometowns Are Not Considered to Have Left Military Service 66

Ministry of Finance Investigates Imported Foreign Rice 73

Since the Ministry of Finance established the National Grain Transportation and Sales Bureau, its task is to purchase and sell rice, prepare warehousing, regulate transportation, and investigate the quantity of production and sales in various provinces. However, purchasing and sales, preparing warehousing, and transportation require sufficient financial preparation in advance, and small-scale operations are ineffective. It has now entrusted the Central Bank to first handle the investigation portion. The Bank of China, the Bank of Communications, and other branches in various places will provide assistance. After the investigation yields results, warehousing and regulating transportation will be prepared, and finally, the purchase and sale can be discussed. The headquarters will be located in Shanghai, and branches or offices will be established in important grain-producing ports throughout the country. (20th Special Dispatch)

Zhang Ji Returns to Peiping from Shaanxi; Plans to Raise Funds to Repair the Yellow Emperor's Mausoleum; Tobacco Suppression in Shaanxi Yields Good Results 109

Peiping Correspondence: Zhang Ji, Central Committee Member of the Kuomintang and Chairman of the Preparatory Committee for the Capital Construction of Xi'an, arrived in Peiping on the evening of the 17th from Xi'an after visiting the Yellow Emperor's Mausoleum. This reporter visited him on the morning of the 18th to inquire about the National Tomb Sweeping Day and the recent situation in Shaanxi Province. The following is a record of Zhang's remarks: "Since the beginning of spring in Shaanxi Province, rainfall has been timely and abundant, with a total of ten thorough rainfalls. The wheat seedlings are lush and thriving, and a bumper harvest is expected this autumn. The Central Government's National Tomb Sweeping Day, commemorating the Mausoleums of the Zhou Dynasty, Mao Mausoleum, and the Yellow Emperor's Mausoleum, aims to awaken the public, remember our Han ancestors, and promote our national spirit. Xi'an is about four hundred li from the Yellow Emperor's Mausoleum. A direct automobile road has been built and traffic will be convenient for next spring's Tomb Sweeping Day, and more people will participate. The Yellow Emperor Temple is located on a high mountain, about 1,200 to 3,000 meters above sea level. The temple has suffered considerable damage because of its age and lack of protection. We have begun to raise funds for repairs. The cypress forest near the Yellow Emperor's Mausoleum is vast and magnificent. The cypresses are relics from two thousand years ago, and those who enter the area feel the hardship of our ancestors' pioneering efforts. The area near the Yellow Emperor's Mausoleum is rich in resources, such as wool and coal mines. However, the 23 counties surrounding the Yellow Emperor's Mausoleum have a population of about one million. The area is vast and sparsely populated, and goods are left unused because of a lack of development. Also, inconvenience of transportation has left the nation paying little attention to this. The authorities believe that it is necessary to actively promote development. The decided steps include local development and immigration. With a little time, these will become reality. As a result of the Shaanxi Provincial Highway Economic Committee's efforts, approximately 2,000 li of roads have been completed. The Xi'an to Lanzhou section will be open to traffic on May 1st. The Xi'an to Hanzhong section, over 1,000 li long, will also be completed soon. The rampant banditry in northern Shaanxi was purely due to the sparse population, allowing bandits to gather easily. Furthermore, the terrain is dangerous, which the bandits use as a stronghold. The people have no ability to defend or resist, causing the bandit forces to grow. Since the arrival of the North China Military Council's staff to Shaanxi to supervise the suppression of bandits, there have been outstanding results. Xu Xiangqian's remaining bandit troops have fled back to Sichuan. The remaining bandits have become feeble, and their elimination is foreseeable. The Shaanxi Provincial Government's tobacco suppression plan has yielded satisfactory results after the first phase of implementation. Farmers in the tobacco-prohibited areas who switched to growing cotton last year had a harvest of about 30 million yuan. Therefore, farmers in other tobacco-growing areas have heard the news and are switching to cotton this year, as it is more profitable than growing tobacco. Therefore, they are following good advice. In terms of the current situation, not only can tobacco seedlings be completely eliminated as scheduled, but the rural economy of Shaanxi Province can also be revitalized and become better. The purpose of building a secondary capital is twofold: (1) to showcase historical sites, and at the same time, local construction will progress with the establishment of the secondary capital, making Xi'an a great tourist area. Its future prosperity can be imagined. (2) Xi'an was the ancient capital of emperors and is of great importance. The construction of the secondary capital is closely related to the development of the Northwest. The people should work together to achieve this goal," and so on. It is heard that Zhang will stay in Peiping for a few days before leaving for the capital. (18th)

The Tragic Situation in Lihuang County, Anhui Province - Parents Starved to Death, Their Son Cut and Cooked Their Flesh 110

Anqing Correspondence: The Anhui Provincial Government recently approved a letter from Liang Guanying, Commander-in-Chief of the Twenty-fifth Route Army, which stated that, according to investigations conducted in the front lines, several months ago, a disaster victim near Dingjiabu was cut and eaten by his son. The tragic situation is unbearable to read, and the address and name are very accurate and not false. Attached is the original report, asking for review. It is noted that three batches of relief grain have been allocated to Lihuang County, totaling 2,800 shi, plus 800 shi of work-relief grain. However, the disaster in the county is severe, and it is only a drop in the bucket, making it difficult to provide relief. A special letter has been sent to the Provincial Disaster Relief Committee for verification and swift relief to save the remaining survivors. The following is the original report, issued in Dingjiabu on March 17: (1) On the afternoon of the 15th of this month, I went to Pengjiawan near Dingjiabu to investigate. I heard a refugee, Zhang Zhangshi, say that there was a Wang Zhangshi (41 years old), a refugee from Zengjiagui, Tangchong. Her husband, named Wudao, had died long ago, and she and her two sons begged for food to survive. They traveled to Liaojia Wawu in Nanxi and temporarily stayed there. In mid-January, when it snowed heavily, they were unable to beg for food. The woman starved to death there. Her two sons, the elder named Wang Dingzhi (12 years old) and the younger Wang Xiaoer (9 years old), had not eaten a grain of rice for several days and were starving and freezing. They became mentally deranged and cut off their mother's leg with a knife, cooked it, and ate it. Zhang Zhangshi claimed that the Wang Zhangshi who was eaten was her sister. She went to see her sister after hearing of her death and personally saw her two nephews cutting the flesh. After hearing this, I was filled with pity. I inquired about the whereabouts of the two sons. They had gone far away to beg for food and were nowhere to be found. (2) On the morning of the 16th of this month, I went to Pengjiawan again and saw Wu Zicheng, who is from Gongjiawan, Zimu River. He had been a soldier under Tian Zijin in the Laomaodong Defense Corps. He said that last year, in October, he saw Wen Yuanyou (40 years old), who had two sons and was from Caijiawan near Maiyuan in the fifth district. Because of the widespread famine, they had no way to beg for food and starved to death. His two sons, the elder named Wen Yousheng (12 years old) and the younger Wen Hesheng (8 years old), were young and starving and cut the flesh off their father's corpse with a kitchen knife and cooked it on the fire. I (Wu Zicheng himself) and the soldiers in the same team had all seen it when we went out on patrol. Later, I heard that both sons had also starved to death. Report by Yue Weigao (March 18).

Guangdong Province's Commercial Control; Rubber and Match Industries Implement Control One After Another; Department of Finance Revises Commercial Control Regulations 111

Guangzhou Correspondence: Commerce in Guangdong Province has declined in recent years, and the number of store closures has increased. According to a survey in March of this year, in Guangzhou alone, a total of 39 businesses closed. The Municipal Chamber of Commerce, seeking a temporary solution, proposed a trade control plan. With the rise of this proposal, merchants who have suffered from competition have occasionally supported it. For example, the Rubber Industry Association recently requested official approval to implement a rubber industry control plan, first by limiting production and then by leveling prices and material standards. A limited council was established to take charge of the matter, with one representative from each factory serving as a director. It was established yesterday. Next, the match industry recently implemented control, stipulating that from April 1 of this year, the Business Tax Bureau will stop issuing new business licenses for match factories. The suspension will last until December 1938. During this period, only match factories that have already registered will be allowed to operate. Those who apply for new business licenses will be prohibited. Other industries that have followed suit and requested control include the hotel and shipping industries. After receiving the reports, the Department of Construction scheduled a meeting on the 15th of this month, gathering shipping representatives to discuss shipping control measures. The measures were drafted by shipping companies, discussed, and then submitted to the Department of Construction for review. The hotel industry, like the rubber and match industries, is now requesting control measures. The number of new hotels is increasing every year, leading to oversupply. Currently, some hotels are reducing room rates by 60% to 50% in order to attract customers, but it is difficult to maintain operations. They have requested the Department of Construction to implement control measures, similar to those in the rubber and match industries, by first limiting new establishments and then standardizing room rates for the entire industry in order to save the business.

As for the commercial control regulations proposed by the Municipal Chamber of Commerce some time ago, they were submitted to the Department of Finance, which dispatched eight specialists to review the commercial control proposal and approved it with revisions. The commercial control regulations are attached below: (Article 1) The Guangdong Provincial Government, in order to revitalize the province's industry and develop the economy, will reorganize and control the province's (city's) chambers of commerce and all commercial firms. (Article 2) The chamber of commerce is subordinate to all commercial firms within the province (city). (Article 3) Each commercial firm will be a unit for selling one or several common commodities. All stores in the province (city) that sell the same commodity will be members of that commercial firm. (Article 4) The organization of each commercial firm is as follows: (1) Six to ten representatives elected by the members of the firm in the province (city). (2) Two to four representatives elected by the producers of the goods sold by the firm (agriculture, industry, commerce, forestry, mining, fishing). (3) One technical expert designated by the government for the goods sold. (4) One economic expert designated by the Provincial Economic Planning Committee. (5) One representative elected by the Provincial (City) General Chamber of Commerce to which the firm belongs. (Article 5) The organization of the Provincial (City) General Chamber of Commerce is as follows: (1) One representative elected by each commercial firm within the province (city). Larger businesses may elect one to three representatives. (2) One technical expert designated by the government. (3) One economic expert designated by the Provincial Economic Planning Committee. (Article 6) The duties of each commercial firm are as follows: (1) To investigate and collect statistics on the production volume, sales volume, production costs, transportation costs, operating costs, market prices, purchasing power, and all other events related to the business of the firm. (2) To study and plan the rationalization and scientificization of the production, transportation, operation, and management of the firm's goods. (3) To unite and mediate events among the various businesses of the same firm. (4) To handle common events among the various firms. (5) To handle matters entrusted by the government. (Article 7) The duties of the Provincial (City) General Chamber of Commerce are as follows: (1) To investigate and collect statistics on the various businesses of the province (city). (2) To study and design the various businesses of the province (city). (3) To promote the joint cooperation of the various commercial firms of the province (city). (4) To control and guide the province (city). (Article 8) The expenses of each commercial firm will be determined by the firms themselves. (Article 9) The technical and economic experts designated by the Provincial Government and the Economic Planning Committee shall submit the prepared plans to the Provincial Government for review and implementation on a monthly basis. (Article 10) These regulations will be promulgated and implemented by the Provincial Government. (April 13)

Reasons for the Destruction of the Tianmashan Police Station 113

Regarding the case of the Tianmashan Public Security Seventh Substation being destroyed by workers from Jiangbei a few days ago, Director He sent Yang Shijie, the leader of the detective team, and a special task force to the countryside to investigate. It is now known that the substation was destroyed by a riot of stone quarrying workers from Chenshan, because new teahouses were opened in Chenshan Town, where stone quarrying workers gathered to gamble. Officer Xu received a report, ordered the police to arrest ten gamblers, and fined each of them. The workers, relying on their numbers, held a grudge and incited a riot, causing injury to Zhou, and the damage to the items in the substation was minor. Afterwards, team leader Yang arrested the two main culprits, who were temporarily bailed out by the stone quarrying foremen to await summons. Team leader Yang reported the situation to the review and seized control.

Suzhou: Various Industries Request Reduction in Business Tax Rates 114

The Wu County Business Tax Bureau has been ordered to review account books, which various industries find unsatisfactory. They have requested the Chamber of Commerce to negotiate with the bureau. After several contacts between the County Chamber of Commerce and Director Guo, a compromise has been agreed upon. However, the silk, oil, wine, bean cake, southern goods, and Chinese and foreign cloth industries associations jointly submitted a request to the County Chamber of Commerce yesterday (20th), requesting that the tax bureau be asked to reduce tax rates due to the decline in commerce. They also requested the establishment of a Business Tax Evaluation Committee. The County Chamber of Commerce decided to submit the above two matters to the joint meeting of the supervisory committee of the Provincial Chamber of Commerce today (21st) for discussion.

Wujiang: Stamp Tax Declarations Returned for Correction 115

The county chamber of commerce processed the registration of old stamp tax stamps. A total of 305 stores made declarations. Now, the Jiangsu Stamp, Tobacco, and Alcohol Tax Bureau of the Ministry of Finance has issued an order stating that the applications of the stores have not been stamped by the review committee and that 136 of the applications have fillings that are not in compliance. They should be returned for correction. Forty-six stores have applications that should not be registered and should be returned, cancelling the registration and completing the amended declaration forms. They must be submitted to the bureau by the end of this month, otherwise they will be invalid. The county chamber of commerce has already taken action.

Wuxi: General Inspection of Social Education Institutions 116

The Education Bureau of this county held its 33rd bureau meeting the day before yesterday, chaired by Director Zang. The following are the important cases decided: (1) Compiling local textbooks. The editors will be paid approximately five yuan per lesson for their contributions. The printing cost is 2,500 yuan. The estimated cost per book is 5 fen. 50,000 copies will be printed each time. After printing, the bureau will distribute them. (2) Dealing with private schools. Each education committee will inspect private schools by May 15th, according to the private school survey form. (3) A general inspection of social education institutions throughout the county will be the central task for May. (4) The bureau will conduct random tests on student performance this academic year. The director will temporarily designate the schools, grades, and subjects, and send personnel to administer the tests.

Request to Dispatch Patrol Boats to Inspect Dry Cocoons 117

Cai Jingde, director of the Wuxi office of the Jiangsu Provincial Cocoon Industry Improvement Management Committee, stated that the silk season is approaching. It is necessary to plan in advance to prevent the smuggling of dry cocoons and to inspect transportation. Yesterday, he submitted a special request to the Department of Construction, asking it to order the dispatch of seven water patrol boats for use. Five of them will be stationed at the major waterways of this county, and two will be transferred from Suzhou and stationed permanently in that county to facilitate mutual communication and assistance.

Zhenjiang: Disaster Victims in the Ninth District Eager to Borrow Seeds 118

The northwest villages of the county have suffered consecutive years of famine. Wang Boling, Magistrate Ma, and representatives of various charitable organizations conducted on-the-spot disaster surveys. They recognized that the disaster victims were unable to purchase seeds and would be disappointed with the autumn harvest. They purchased seeds to lend to poor households. Over 4,300 disaster victims in the ninth district applied to borrow seeds. The district worked overnight to prepare the list. The county government issued seed loan certificates, and over a thousand households went to Yang to collect seeds daily.

Yangzhou: Transfer of Sha Tian Official Property Files to the County 119

The Jiangdu County Government, due to the provincial government's decision to abolish the provincial Sha Tian Official Property Bureau and transfer it to the county governments, received a provincial order yesterday (18th) ordering it to appoint a suitable staff member to receive all files regarding the Sha Tian official property within Jiangdu County. Magistrate Ma appointed section member Pi Zhongyi to go to the Zhenjiang Sha Tian Official Property Bureau to negotiate the transfer.

Changshu: Merchants Request Lenient Penalties for Failure to Affix Stamps 120

In this county, stamp duties were usually collected by the Stamp Bureau. Now, the bureau has been abolished, and the county government is handling the duties. Because county government officials are imposing excessively harsh penalties, the merchants have requested the County Chamber of Commerce to make an appeal for lenient treatment in order to alleviate their difficulties. The general idea of the appeal is that the Stamp Tax Bureau used to form an adjudication committee with the Chamber of Commerce and the Public Security Bureau to handle cases of failure to affix stamps. The committee usually dealt with these cases leniently, ordering the purchase of some stamp tickets. The merchants' failure to affix stamps was usually due to temporary negligence and not comparable to intentional tax evasion for petty gain. Now, commerce is declining day by day. Since stamp duties are now handled by the county government, in terms of law, the business community is accustomed to the previous practice and is mostly unaware of the severity of the penalties for failure to follow the regulations. In terms of business conditions, occasional negligence is forgivable. All industries are withering away, and it seems that extra leniency should be given to merchants who occasionally fail to affix stamps. This would show generosity and alleviate the hardships of the merchants.

Special Report

Investigation into the Auxiliary Currency of Gansu 121

— Zhu Jingzhou

(I) Overview

Gansu Province, with its inconvenient transportation and stagnant financial situation, only circulated silver taels and copper coins during the late Qing Dynasty. Silver coins and copper coins were not in circulation. In the third year of the Republic of China (1914), Zhang Guangjian was ordered to govern Gansu, and he brought a large amount of copper coins. From then on, Gansu Province had the name of copper coins. This article, although titled "Auxiliary Currency," only focuses on copper coins. Initially, they only circulated in the provincial capital, and only those worth ten cash were used. Each national currency yuan could be exchanged for about one hundred copper coins (that is, about one thousand cash). This maintained the decimal price. However, this also led to the increasing influx of foreign copper coins. In the ninth year of the Republic of China (1920), Lu Hongtao succeeded as the governor of Gansu. At that time, the Gansu Official Bank was experiencing a run. Lu Hongtao, in order to relieve the market and cope with the military expenses, initiated the casting of copper coins. Unfortunately, he entrusted the task to the wrong people. The copper quality was inferior, and the casting method was extremely crude. People at the time called them "sand-mold copper coins." Although the government tried to promote them by force, the high price of copper coins and the exclusive casting of those worth ten cash proved unprofitable. So they changed to casting those worth twenty cash, in order to gain more profit. Cunning people, envious of the lucrative profits and the ease of imitating the model, set up private furnaces for private minting, resulting in a sharp drop in prices. The Lanzhou market became a world of sand-mold copper coins. Not only were good coins driven out completely, but all the copper coins in the counties were also melted down. At that time, the financial situation was chaotic, everything was expensive, agriculture and commerce were in distress, and complaints arose everywhere. Lu Hongtao deeply regretted his past mistakes. He began to collect all the sand-mold copper coins in the market at the rate of twenty strings per tael of silver and destroy them. At the same time, he purchased several small printing machines from Tianjin, re-refined the collected sand-mold coins, and re-cast them into copper coins worth ten cash, until the sand-mold copper coins were completely collected. At the same time, Kong Fanjin, the garrison commander of Longnan, also purchased large-scale machinery from Tianjin and Shanghai, and set up a factory to cast them at Quan'shui. Because there was no profit to be made from copper coins worth ten cash, he imitated the Sichuan currency format and cast those worth fifty, one hundred, and two hundred cash. Some were even worth dozens or hundreds of strings of cash, collectively called "big plates." The people of Longnan, under the pressure of accumulated power, had no way to resist and had to endure the promotion of these coins. By the fourteenth year of the Republic of China (1925), when the National Revolutionary Army entered Gansu, Kong Fanjin was forced to leave Qin, and the poison of these "big plate" copper coins had spread throughout the counties of Longnan. After Kong left, the National Revolutionary Army transported all the machinery to the provincial capital (the machinery of the current mint). They once tried to cast copper coins worth one hundred cash, intending to promote them in the provincial capital, but were stopped by the Chamber of Commerce. However, the area of circulation of the "big plate" copper coins has since become wider, from Longnan to Longdong, and to Lintao, Dingxi, Yuzhong, and other counties, almost without exception. This was because of the bankruptcy of the rural areas and the depletion of finances, leaving no other means of circulation. In the twenty-first year of the Republic of China (1932), the provincial mint also handed over more than 200,000 catties of copper coins to the Ping City Official Money Bureau for distribution, along with old "big plate" copper coins. At the same time, Bu Yunxiang of Xijin Nanhang also transported a large amount of copper coins and handed them over to the mint to be re-cast into "man-plate" copper coins and transported to the Hezhou area for promotion, causing prices to skyrocket and the people's livelihood to deteriorate. Later, with the approval of the Provincial Finance Department, all casting was stopped. The 66,500 "one hundred cash" copper coins that had already been cast were sold by the Ping City Bureau in Hezhou, Jingning, Huining, and other places. This is a general overview of the casting of copper coins in Gansu Province. In the past two years, although Gansu Province has long stopped casting, it is easier for copper coins worth one hundred and five hundred from nearby Sichuan to flow into the Longnan area. Efforts are currently being made to prohibit them. However, if Kong had not started it, these inferior coins might not have been so easy to invade. Tracing the source of the disaster, I cannot but hold Kong responsible.

(II) Summary of the Investigation

When Jingzhou first took office, he considered the relationship between auxiliary currency and the people's livelihood to be extremely close. He urgently wanted to find a way to rectify the situation, in order to gradually bring it into order. Therefore, in September of the twenty-third year of the Republic of China (1934), he created a form and ordered all counties to investigate and report on the circulation of copper coins in their local areas, so as to understand the truth and serve as a preliminary step for rectification. The main items listed in the survey form are as follows: (1) What is the total number of large copper coins (such as those worth twenty, fifty, one hundred, etc.) circulating in the county market? What is the exchange rate for silver dollars? (For example, how many ten-cash, twenty-cash, fifty-cash, and one-hundred-cash copper coins can be exchanged for one silver dollar?) (2) Where do these large copper coins come from? If prohibited, would there be any impact on the market? (3) What is the impact of the circulation of these large copper coins on the livelihood of the general poor? (4) In addition to the above-mentioned copper coins, what other currencies are most popular in the market? Do other merchants and money shops issue similar promissory notes for circulation? What are the quantities? What are the exchange rates? All of the above items were divided and ordered to each county to investigate and report truthfully, and they were also asked to express their opinions on the rectification, for reference. Currently, sixty-two counties have responded to the hall. The main points of the investigation are summarized below.

(A) Types of Copper Coins Circulating in Various Counties

According to the investigation reports, the types of copper coins circulating in the counties can be divided into five types: those worth ten, twenty, fifty, one hundred, and two hundred cash. Among them, the ones that occupy the widest area are the ten-cash and one-hundred-cash copper coins, which circulate in thirty-four counties. The next most common are the fifty-cash copper coins, which circulate in thirty-two counties. The twenty-cash copper coins are the next most common, circulating in twenty-four counties. The two-hundred-cash copper coins only circulate in eight counties. The types of copper coins commonly used in each county are even more complex. The counties that commonly use ten-cash, twenty-cash, fifty-cash, and one-hundred-cash copper coins include Weiyuan, Jingning, Longde, Longxi, and Minxian. The counties that commonly use twenty-cash, fifty-cash, and one-hundred-cash copper coins include Dingxi, Qingyang, and Yuzhong. The counties that commonly use ten-cash and twenty-cash copper coins include Linxia, Gulang, Yongdeng, Tao'sha, Jingyuan, Wuwei, Xiahe, Yongjing, Lintan, Hezheng, Lintao, Gao'lan, and Jingtai. The counties that commonly use fifty-cash and one-hundred-cash copper coins include Jingchuan, Zhangxian, Huaping, Qingshui, Gangu, Zhuanglang, Xihe, Huating, Haiyuan, Wushan, Chongxin, Huining, Zhenyuan, Qin'an, Lixian, and Lingtai. The counties that commonly use ten-cash copper coins include Linze, Ningding, Zhangye, Minle, Shandan, Yumen, Jinta, Anxi, Jiaohuang, Yongchang, Gaotai, Dingxin, Jiuquan, and Mindong. Only Liang county commonly uses ten-cash, twenty-cash, and one-hundred-cash copper coins. The counties that commonly use fifty-cash, one-hundred-cash, and two-hundred-cash copper coins include Kangxian, Wudu, Liangdang, Chengxian, and Tianshui. Huanxian commonly uses fifty-cash and one-hundred-cash copper coins. Wenxian commonly uses two-hundred-cash copper coins. The counties of Xigu and Huixian commonly use twenty-cash, fifty-cash, one-hundred-cash and two-hundred-cash copper coins. Tongwei county commonly uses one-hundred-cash copper coins.

(B) Quantity of Copper Coins Circulating in Various Counties

Regarding the quantity of copper coins circulating in various counties, with the exception of Gulang, Shui Deng, Tao Sha, Jingyuan, Wuwei, Linze, Ningding, Lintan, Hezheng, Zhangye, Minle, Longde, Shandan, Yumen, Jinta, Lintao, Qingyang, Anxi, Jiaohuang, Tianshui, Kangxian, Wudu, Qin'an, Shui Chang, Tongxiao, Xigu, Gao'lan, Dingxin, Jiuquan, and Lingtai, thirty counties that, due to special circumstances, could not be investigated or estimated, according to the reported quantities, Minxian, Wenxian, and Huating each have 2,000,000 strings (each string is equivalent to 1,000 copper cash. This article generally uses strings as the unit, following the common usage in various counties). Huixian has 77,000 strings, Huining has 70,000 strings, Jingtai has 50,000 strings, Qingshui has 35,000 strings, Zhangxian and Longxi each have 20,000 strings, Jingchuan has 15,000 strings, Linxia has 14,400 strings, Jingning, Gaotai and Chengxian each have 10,000 strings, Pingliang, Wushan, and Yuzhong each have 8,000 strings, Xiahe, Haiyuan, and Zhenyuan each have 6,000 strings, Ganggu county has 5,000 strings, Weiyuan county has 4,000 strings, Liangdang and Chongxin counties each have 3,000 strings, Minle, Xihe, and Yongjing each have 2,000 strings, Dingxi has 1,500 strings, Zhuanglang county has 1,340 strings, Xun county has 680 strings, Huaping has 300 strings, Jie county has 100 strings. The total for the above thirty-two counties is 998,320 strings. Each county has an average of 31,197 strings and 500 cash in common copper coins, equivalent to about 4,400 or 4,500 silver dollars. (To be continued)

Local News

The Bank of Communications Held its Shareholders' Meeting Yesterday; Approved an Increase in Capital Stock of 20 Million; Government Shares at 12 Million, Commercial Shares at 8 Million; Board of Directors to Elect Standing Directors Tomorrow 122

The Bank of Communications convened a shareholders' meeting at the Bankers' Association on Hong Kong Road yesterday at 2:00 PM, chaired by Hu Bijiang. The meeting approved an increase of 10 million in government shares, re-elected commercial shareholder supervisors, and the Ministry of Finance appointed the list of government shareholder directors and supervisors. It was decided that a board of directors meeting would be held tomorrow at 2:00 PM to elect standing directors. The current Chairman Hu Bijiang and General Manager Tang Shoumin are expected to be re-elected. Details are as follows:

Meeting Agenda

The agenda of yesterday's meeting was as follows: (1) Ringing the bell to open the meeting; (2) Paying the highest respect to the flag of the Party, the nation, and the portrait of Sun Yat-sen; (3) The Chairman respectfully reading Sun Yat-sen's will, followed by three minutes of silence; (4) The Chairman delivering the opening remarks; (5) Reporting and discussing the business situation of 1934 and the distribution of final account interest, and re-electing commercial shareholder supervisors; (6) Adjournment. Attendees yesterday included Hu Bijiang, Tang Shoumin, Qian Xinzhi, Chen Xing, Zhang Shouyong, Qin Shize, Xu Xiuzhi, Yu Baoxuan, Hu Zutong, Li Chengyi, and over a hundred others. Zou Lin, Vice Minister of the Ministry of Finance, Xu Keting, Director of the Currency Department, and Song Ziliang, General Manager of the China Construction Bank, were specially dispatched by the Ministry of Finance to attend and supervise.

Declaration of Meeting Commencement

At precisely 2:00 PM, the shareholders had gathered one after another. Chairman Hu Bijiang reported that according to Article 56 of the bank's articles of association, the shareholders' meeting could not be held unless shareholders representing more than one-third of the total shares were present. The total shares of the bank amounted to 8,715,650 yuan, and the shareholders present represented 3,580,200 yuan, exceeding one-third (calculated as 2,905,216 yuan), so the meeting could proceed. (After the meeting commenced, an additional 1,354,000 yuan worth of shares arrived, bringing the total to 4,934,200 yuan).

Adoption of Resolutions

After the Chairman declared the meeting open, bank employee Zhuang Shuhao first reported on the general business accounts for 1934, followed by Supervisor Xu Xiuzhi's report on the audit of the accounts. Immediately proposals were put forward, including (1) the profit distribution plan for 1934, (2) the proposal to set aside a savings reserve fund, and (3) the proposal to re-elect commercial shareholder supervisors, all of which were passed. The four commercial shareholder supervisors to be elected were then elected by the commercial shareholders present through separate voting. After the ballots were cast, the Chairman announced that due to temporarily important motions, which needed to be raised first, the opening of the ballot box was temporarily delayed. He then reported on (1) the proposal to increase government shares by 10 million yuan for retroactive approval, (2) the proposal to request the Ministry of Finance to promulgate approved amended regulations, and (3) the proposal to amend the draft articles of association for approval, explaining that the Ministry of Finance's increase in government shares was related to the overall financial situation and greatly protected the rights of the bank's commercial shareholders. Therefore, the amended regulations and articles of association contained many preferential points. The full text of the amended regulations and articles of association was then read out item by item, and all were passed without objection.

Election of Supervisors

Subsequently, shareholders appointed supervisors and vote counters to oversee the counting of votes and the calculation of share rights. As a result, Ye Chongxun with 3669 votes, Wen Xiangchen with 3370 votes, Zou Minchu with 3112 votes, and Jia Shiyi with 2876 votes were elected as commercial shareholder supervisors. Wang Zigang with 850 votes and Wang Youling with 411 votes were elected as alternate supervisors.

Government Shareholder Directors and Supervisors

After the increase in government shares, according to the amended regulations, the number of directors should be 21, with 9 government shares and 12 commercial shares. The number of supervisors should be 7, with 3 government shares and 4 commercial shares. The Ministry of Finance has already appointed Wang Rutang, Song Ziliang, Yang Dunfu, Xu Xinliu, Yang Xiaotian, Shen Shuyu, Zhang Shouyong, Li Chengyi, and Qin Zuze as the nine government shareholder directors, and Xu Xiuzhi, Zhang Xiaolin, and Zhao Dihua as the three government shareholder supervisors. The term of office for the commercial shareholder directors has not yet expired, and they remain Hu Yun, Tang Shoumin, Qian Yongming, Hu Zutong, Chen Xing, Zhou Zuomin, Li Ming, Wang Chengzu, Chen Huide, Ye Xun, Yang Desen, and Zhang Jia'ao.

Board Meeting Tomorrow

After the bank's organization is expanded and government shareholder directors and supervisors are added, the first board meeting will be held tomorrow (Monday) at 2:00 PM on the third floor of the bank on the Bund of Sanma Road. The newly added government shareholder directors will all be present. At that time, seven standing directors will be mutually elected in accordance with Article 14 of the amended regulations, and the Ministry of Finance will appoint one of the standing directors as the chairman. The chairman will then consult with the standing directors to appoint one general manager from among the directors. It is rumored that the current Chairman Hu Yun and General Manager Tang Shoumin are expected to be re-elected.

Amended Regulations

The Ministry of Finance's amended regulations for the Bank of Communications are as follows: Article 1. The Bank of Communications, with the special permission of the National Government, is a bank for the development of national industries, established as a joint-stock company. Article 2. The capital stock of the Bank of Communications is fixed at 20 million yuan of national currency, divided into 300,000 shares, each share valued at 100 yuan of national currency. Government shares are 120,000 shares, and commercial shares are 80,000 shares, all paid up in one installment. If it is necessary to increase commercial shares, it may be decided by the shareholders' meeting and submitted to the Ministry of Finance for approval. Article 3. The Bank of Communications shall have its head office in Shanghai and establish branches in places necessary for industry, or enter into agency contracts with other banks. Article 4. The shares of the Bank of Communications shall all be registered and shall be limited to those with the nationality of the Republic of China. Article 5. The business term of the Bank of Communications shall be 30 years from the date of promulgation of these regulations. Upon expiration, it may be decided by the shareholders' meeting and extended with the approval of the Ministry of Finance. Article 6. The dividends of the Bank of Communications shall be 5% per annum for government shares and 7% per annum for commercial shares. Article 7. At least one-tenth of the total net profit from annual business operations must be set aside as a reserve fund before dividends and bonuses can be distributed. The order of distribution is to pay commercial shareholder dividends first, followed by government shareholder dividends. If there is still a surplus, the bonuses are distributed equally on a per-share basis. The appropriation of the aforementioned reserve fund and dividends and bonuses shall be reported to the Ministry of Finance for record after being approved by the shareholders' meeting. Article 8. The use of the reserve fund is to cover capital losses and maintain the average of dividends. Article 9. The Bank of Communications, entrusted by the government and the Central Bank, shall handle the following matters: (1) Underwriting government bonds and managing the repayment of principal and interest; (2) Acting as an agent for public industrial institutions to issue bonds and manage the repayment of principal and interest; (3) Acting as an agent for the disbursement of public funds for transportation projects; (4) Handling other matters related to encouraging and developing industries; (5) Managing a portion of the national treasury. Article 10. With the special permission of the Ministry of Finance, the Bank of Communications may issue convertible notes, but must comply with the regulations on convertible notes. Article 11. The types of business operations of the Bank of Communications are as follows: (1) Managing the underwriting or acceptance of corporate bonds issued by industrial companies; (2) Providing loans secured by reliable collateral and providing current loans for industrial and commercial enterprises; (3) Providing loans secured by movable and immovable property for industrial purposes, but the total amount of loans shall not exceed one-half of the paid-up capital; (4) Discounting or purchasing commercial bills and drafts with definite maturity dates; (5) Accepting various deposits and safekeeping securities, bills, and all other valuables on behalf of others; (6) Trust and savings business; (7) Acting as an agent for collecting and disbursing various funds; (8) Domestic and foreign remittances and cargo mortgages; (9) Buying and selling securities, raw gold and silver, and foreign currencies; (10) Treasury transportation and insurance business; (11) Investing in the development of industries, but the amount of investment shall not exceed one-quarter of the paid-up capital. Article 12. In addition to the various types of business operations listed in Article 11, the Bank of Communications shall not engage in the following and other businesses: (1) Various unsecured loans and guarantees; (2) Purchasing its own shares and providing loans secured by its own shares; (3) Buying and selling real estate, but real estate necessary for business operations is not subject to this restriction. Article 13. The Bank of Communications shall have 21 directors and 7 supervisors, with the Ministry of Finance appointing 9 directors and 3 supervisors. The remaining 12 directors and 4 supervisors shall be elected by commercial shareholders in the shareholders' meeting from among commercial shareholders with 100 or more shares. The term of office for directors is four years, and the term of office for supervisors is three years, and both may be re-elected upon expiration. Article 14. The Bank of Communications shall have 7 standing directors, elected by the directors. The Ministry of Finance shall appoint one of the standing directors as the chairman. The Bank of Communications shall have one general manager, selected by the chairman in consultation with the standing directors from among the directors, and appointed with the approval of the board of directors and reported to the Ministry of Finance for record. Article 15. The shareholders' meeting of the Bank of Communications shall be divided into the following two types: (1) Regular shareholders' meeting; (2) Extraordinary shareholders' meeting. Article 16. The regular shareholders' meeting shall be held once a year at the location of the head office, convened by the board of directors. Article 17. When the board of directors believes that important matters require a meeting, it may convene an extraordinary shareholders' meeting. Article 18. When more than half of the directors, or all of the supervisors, or 50 or more members of the shareholders' meeting holding 10% or more of the total shares, request a meeting due to important matters, an extraordinary shareholders' meeting may be convened. Article 19. When the shareholders' meeting is held, shareholders with 10 or more shares or representatives of 10 or more shares who have registered 60 days before the meeting are eligible to be members and attend the meeting. Article 20. The voting rights of members of the shareholders' meeting are one vote for every 10 shares, and for 100 or more shares, one additional vote is added for every 20 shares. Article 21. When a commercial shareholder member of the shareholders' meeting is unable to attend the meeting due to an accident, their authorized agent shall be limited to members. Article 22. If the Bank of Communications violates these regulations and the articles of association of the bank, or events detrimental to the government occur, the Ministry of Finance may stop them. Article 23. The Bank of Communications shall formulate detailed articles of association in accordance with the main purpose of these regulations, submit them to the shareholders' meeting for resolution, and submit them to the Ministry of Finance for approval and record. The same shall apply to any revisions or additions. Article 24. Matters not stipulated in these regulations shall be handled in accordance with the Company Law. Article 25. When these regulations are to be amended, they may be resolved by the shareholders' meeting and submitted by the chairman to the Ministry of Finance for approval and amendment. Article 26. These regulations shall be implemented from the date of promulgation.

As for the loss items, various expenses amounted to over 3,088,000 yuan, which is about the same as last year. Various amortizations amounted to over 716,000 yuan, bad debts amounted to over 120,000 yuan, and issuance tax amounted to over 328,000 yuan, with total losses amounting to over 4,254,000 yuan. In addition, the net profit of the bank's savings department in 1934 was over 86,000 yuan, an increase of over 6,000 yuan compared to 1933. Revitalizing the Rural Areas; Spring Plowing Movement Begins; Social Affairs Bureau Issues a Letter to Farmers 123

According to Dagongshe, the spring plowing movement prepared by the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau, the Municipal Party Department, the Municipal Farmers' Association, and the Agricultural Experiment Field began yesterday. Farmers' associations in various districts jointly mobilized for publicity, and the Social Affairs Bureau issued a letter to farmers throughout the city, sincerely aiming to revitalize the rural areas. The details are as follows:

Letter from the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau to Farmers

The Municipal Social Affairs Bureau issued a letter to farmers throughout the city yesterday, stating: "Farmers, in recent years, China's rural areas seem to have been plagued by misfortune. Whether it is natural disasters or man-made calamities, they have continuously made farmers poorer and more declining. A few years ago, the various needs of life could still be勉强managed, and there was no worry or anxiety, but now it is different, and there are often worries about 'no clothes to wear,' 'no food to eat,' and 'no place to live.' On the surface, this is a common problem that everyone feels, but the fundamental problem lies in the backwardness of agriculture itself, without new knowledge to prevent disasters and increase production skills. Because of the gradual decline of production, it has affected the bankruptcy of the rural economy, coupled with the heavy exploitation of international capitalism, which has made farmers' lives even more difficult. This is really a serious and terrible thing, not only making the vast rural areas collapse and decline, but even making the entire Chinese nation unable to revive and become strong. However, if we want to revitalize the rural areas, relieve the suffering of farmers, and improve the lives of farmers, it is not a difficult problem. Because the 20th century is the century of science, all undertakings must tend to be rational and scientific. New agriculture has made amazing progress. They use group organization, scientific methods, select seeds, eliminate diseases and insects, harvest agricultural products, irrigate and fertilize, improve cultivation, and even use airplanes to sow seeds and spread insecticide powder, so that the yield of crops is gradually increased, and the lives of farmers are gradually improved, becoming rich and strong countries in the world today. If we want to make our agriculture progress and improve the lives of farmers, we naturally have to use scientific methods, because human strength cannot compete with machinery, and if we want to use scientific methods, we must seek all kinds of new agricultural knowledge to improve the quality of production and increase the quantity of production, so that we can break the current difficult situation of farmers and develop into a realm of peaceful and happy life, prosperous fields and gardens. People, land, and sovereignty are the main elements that make up our country. In China, farmers account for the largest number of people. If every member can make their agriculture progress, and every member can make their lives comfortable, in other words, every member can 'govern themselves and govern others,' 'support themselves and support others,' and 'defend themselves and defend the country,' then it is enhancing a kind of prosperity of the country. The plan for the year lies in spring. Spring is the prelude to the beginning of agricultural cultivation, so now we want to hold a 'spring plowing movement,' which is based on this important meaning to engage in. During the 'spring plowing movement,' we use the method of touring lectures to deeply enter the various rural areas of this city to provide a detailed introduction to various issues that are closely related to farmers, such as seed selection, pest control, crop cultivation, agricultural tool improvement, animal husbandry and feeding, sideline promotion, water conservancy dredging, cooperative promotion, etc., so that farmers can gain an increase in new agricultural knowledge and an improvement in production technology. Therefore, we want to invite our dear farmers to actively participate in this movement. We hope that farmers will work hard to build a new agricultural country."

Farmers' Associations in Various Districts Jointly Mobilize

The Municipal Farmers' Association has already started the spring plowing movement sponsored by the Social Affairs Bureau, and has issued instructions to the Wusong, Jiangwan, Yinxiang, Yinhang, Zhabei, Pengxiao, Zhenru, Pusong, Caojing, Fahua, Hunan, Yangsi, Tangqiao, Yangjing, Lixing, Gaohang, and Gaoqiao branches and offices in the city to organize spring plowing movement touring lecture teams, set off for lectures, designate the executive secretary of each branch as the team leader, lead farmers, and implement general mobilization. At the same time, the Municipal Farmers' Association takes advantage of the spring plowing movement to carry out large-scale literacy publicity in order to enlighten farmers' knowledge. Executive Secretary Yu Zhenhui will set off to guide the various districts today.

Opening Film Screenings; Free Rice Milling

The Spring Plowing Movement Preparatory Committee, in order to instill in farmers the experience and knowledge of various improvement technologies and knowledge such as sowing, seed selection, and pest control, has specially selected several agricultural films from the Central Propaganda Committee and the China Film Association to be screened in various districts. In addition, the Shanghai Machine Factory will use several water pumping boats with new-style domestic rice milling machines installed, and will go to various districts to perform on-site demonstrations and provide free rice milling for farmers.

Engaging Experts to Deliver Lectures

This spring plowing movement is the first time it has been held in the city, so it is expanding publicity and touring lectures. In addition to the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau, the Municipal Party Department, the Municipal Farmers' Association, and the Agricultural Experiment Field, and other four agencies, together with the farmers' sub-associations in various districts and the municipal committee members in each district, serving as lecturers, they have also sent letters to engage more than ten agricultural experts to take turns to give special academic lectures, and compiled and printed publications, leaflets, slogans, etc., which are distributed to farmers to be posted for browsing at any time.

Slogans and Catchphrases for the Spring Plowing Movement

(1) To revitalize the rural areas, we should start with improving agricultural affairs first; (2) To improve agricultural affairs, we must first increase farmers' knowledge; (3) To have a good harvest, we must pay attention to seed selection, pest control, and improved cultivation methods; (4) The spring plowing movement is a movement to instill knowledge in farmers; (5) Grouping the lives of farmers and scientizing agricultural technology; (6) Promoting sideline occupations and promoting cooperation are sufficient to regulate the rural economy; (7) Dredging rivers to facilitate irrigation and building roads to facilitate transportation; (8) The purpose of the spring plowing movement is to revitalize the rural areas; (9) Farmers, come and listen to the lectures of the spring plowing movement; (10) Farmers, let's all get up and organize a new rural area.

Three Banks Confer on Detailed Measures for Relieving Industry and Commerce Loans; After Formulating, Formally Convene a Committee; The Purpose of Loans Focuses on Production 124

According to the Central News Agency, the Central Bank, the Bank of China, and the Bank of Communications, together with the Bankers' Association, have been ordered by the Ministry of Finance to launch a 20 million yuan relief loan for industry and commerce. In recent days, the general managers of the business bureaus of the three banks, Xi Demao, Bei Songsun, and Zhang Peishen, have been conferring on detailed measures, which will be formulated within days, and a committee will be formally convened, and the Bankers' Association will be notified to send representatives to participate. When the relief loans are handled, the committee will preside over them. In addition to the one or two people from each of the three banks, the committee will be composed of two or three people dispatched by the Bankers' Association. Within the committee, investigation and other small groups will be set up. The purpose of this loan is to relieve the economic decline and financial depletion of our country, and relief must be started in the area of production. Loaning to factories is indirectly to revive society, so the loan procedures are very solemn. In addition to investigating its content, the technical aspects of its production must also be guided and improved. The committee will set up investigative organizations for factory content, production conditions, and product sales for factual needs, and designate the borrowing banks to be responsible for them. When necessary, the Municipal Chamber of Commerce and local associations will be asked to assist.

U.S. Economic Mission Telegraphed That They Will Arrive in Shanghai Tomorrow Morning, U.S. Ambassador Going South to Greet Them in Nanjing 129

The Central News Agency reports that the U.S. Economic Survey Mission left Japan the day before yesterday to come to China. The reception office has received the telegram of departure from the mission. U.S. Ambassador Johnson has also come south from Peiping to Shanghai to greet them. However, because the mission will be going to Nanjing the day after their arrival in Shanghai, the reception has been postponed, and the Ambassador will greet them in Nanjing. The Central News Agency reporter has filed the following details:

Telegraph Reports Their Movements

The reception office of the U.S. Economic Survey Mission received a telegram from Japan yesterday morning from Mr. Forbes, the head of the mission, reporting that he himself and all the members of the mission had left Japan on the Dollar Steamship Company's President Harrison ship to come to China. After receiving the telegram, the reception office immediately replied to express their welcome. The President Harrison is scheduled to arrive at 8:30 AM tomorrow morning and will dock at the Dollar Line wharf at Bailianjing, Pudong. The reception office has contacted the Jianghai Customs to arrange for a special launch to pick them up. It is also learned that the reception office held a full executive committee meeting at 5:30 PM the night before last to retroactively appoint staff and discuss important work matters such as the reception itinerary.

List of Members

The members of the mission include Mr. Forbes, the head of the mission, Mr. Carroll, the deputy head, Mr. and Mrs. Story, secretaries, Mr. Shiffley, accountant, Mr. and Mrs. Dollar, Mr. and Mrs. Dillingham, Mr. and Mrs. Condict, Mr. Rogers, Mr. Lemare, Mr. and Mrs. Hutchins, Mr. Campbell, Mr. McNair, Mr. Jones, Mr. Becksbey, Mr. and Mrs. Wickham, etc. As for Mr. Thomas, originally scheduled to participate as honorary deputy head, he was unable to accompany them due to temporary matters. Also, Mr. Feiler, a member of the mission, came to Shanghai a few days ago to arrange the inspection program in China and has already returned to Japan. Mr. Feiler could not accompany them because he had to attend this year's Pacific Science Association held in Tokyo. Other members, Mr. Houlman and Mr. Philip, will join the mission when it arrives in Shanghai.

Brief Biography of the Head

Mr. Forbes graduated from Harvard University in 1892 and received a doctorate in law in 1912. He was in business from 1894 to 1902. Since 1899, he served in the Philippine government, initially in administrative positions. From 1904 to 1908, he served as Vice Governor of the Philippines. From November 1909 to September 1913, he served as Governor of the Philippines. In 1921, U.S. President Harding appointed him as an investigator of the Philippines. In 1931, he served as chairman of the Haiti Investigation Mission. From March of the same year to 1932, he was the U.S. Ambassador to Japan. He is currently the honorary chairman of the U.S.-China Association. Mr. Carroll, the deputy head, graduated from Yale University in 1899. From 1907 to 1913, he served as an engineering consultant in Mexico, engaged in the design and construction of railways, mining, irrigation, and other important projects, and served as the deputy chief engineer of the country's international railways. From 1913 to 1915, he designed and built railways in Cuba and Haiti and continued as an engineering consultant. From 1915 to 1927, he served as the chief engineer of the Hukwang Railways in China. From 1927 to 1933, he served as the director-general and chief engineer of the national railways and the chief surveyor in Persia (Iran).

Purpose of the Inspection

According to the reception office's information, when Mr. Feiler, a member of the inspection mission, came to China to make arrangements a few days ago, he stated that Mr. Forbes, the head of the mission, said that the purpose of this visit to China was to understand the actual situation of our country's construction and the situation of the Far Eastern market. Before obtaining a clear impression after the inspection, he will temporarily not make any statements to the Chinese and foreign press.

The New Life Service Corps, organized by the Shanghai New Life Movement Promotion Association, held a joint meeting of the heads and deputy heads of each subgroup at the Municipal Party Headquarters conference room at 2:00 PM yesterday afternoon. In addition to Lu Jingshi and Cai Jingjun, those present included Mei Hongquan, Chen Zhongfu, Chen Duzhen, Lin Xueyan, Ruan Kaiji, Zhang Mingqin, Chen Baotai, Dai Hongen, Diao Qingen, Wang Chenge, Fu Zhenbei, Wang Dashui, Wang Yonggong, Hu Tianseng, Bao Henian, Shen Yu, Liang Fuchu, Feng Xiancheng, Niu Jingjian, Shen Ding, Hong Zhen, Ling Xianwen, Gu Ruofeng, Shen Liangzhong, Yang Dean, and others, totaling over twenty people.

Resolutions Passed

Lu Jingshi presided over the meeting, and Yang Dean recorded the minutes. The ceremony was conducted as usual. First, the chairman reported the purpose of the meeting and then discussed the agenda items. (1) Regarding the attitude the corps should take towards the recent religious processions and temple fairs, it was resolved that the subgroups should propose concrete measures, which would then be recommended to the New Life Movement Association. (2) Regarding how to ban clothes drying along the street, which is unsightly, it was resolved: (a) To send a letter to the Public Works Department requesting that the construction of three-story racks on rooftops be prohibited, and that future residential buildings should have drying platforms to avoid clothes drying on the roadside. (3) Regarding how to ban street vendors along the roads, it was resolved: To send a letter to the Public Security Bureau requesting that strict bans be enforced on important roads and transportation hubs. (4) Regarding the screening of New Life Movement slogans in movie theaters at the beginning of each showing to raise public awareness, it was resolved: Passed, and recommended to the New Life Movement Association. The rest is omitted. The meeting adjourned at 4:30 PM.

Service Guidelines

"The Third Phase of Service Guidelines of the Youth Service Corps of the Shanghai New Life Movement Promotion Association" includes the following: Rectify the appearance of the city, and clean and tidy up railway stations and wharves. Standards: (1) Clean the walls, doors, and windows thoroughly. (2) All coolies and servants must wear uniforms and be numbered. (3) Travelers getting on and off trains and ships must strictly observe order. (4) Road signs, advertisements, lights, clocks, and sanitary facilities must be well-arranged. (5) Travelers should not shout or joke loudly. (6) Vendors should not sell unclean food. (7) Ticket sales should be fair, with no overcharging or evasion of exchange rates. (8) Unauthorized persons are prohibited from soliciting luggage or arbitrarily extorting money. (Addendum) Pay attention to whether the following matters are in good condition: (1) Whether trains and ships run according to the scheduled time. (2) Whether trains and ships are overloaded with passengers and cargo. (3) Whether the construction of stations and wharves is solid. (4) Whether the staff treats passengers with humility and politeness. (Note) (1) Those who do not meet these standards should be advised to correct them. If there is unreasonable resistance, the police can be notified nearby to reprimand them, and their names and the names of the places should be recorded. (2) The team leader should fill out a report on the above service situation and the opinions of each service, and submit it to the subgroup leader, who will then submit it to the headquarters.

Today's Service

Today is a weekly holiday for the corps and also the date for the members to start serving. Therefore, each subgroup of the corps will distribute armbands to each team leader, who will then distribute them to each member. This afternoon, each team leader will lead the members to set off to serve in various roads, thoroughfares, and alleyways, and begin the third phase of service guidelines. Special attention will be paid to the North and South Railway Stations, as well as the stations in Tiantong'an, Jiangwan, Wusong, Xujiahui, Zhenru, Longhua, and other places, as well as the wharves along the Sixteen Pushi and Suzhou River. Efforts will be made to ensure that they meet the goals of the New Life Movement.

Cadre Training Class of the Municipal Defense Association Holds Live Firing Exercise, Today and Tomorrow at the West Fort, Graduation Ceremony to Be Held in the Middle of Next Month 131

The cadre training class of the Municipal Defense Association has begun training and will hold a graduation ceremony in the middle of next month. Live firing exercises will be held today (the 21st) and tomorrow at the Longhua West Fort. The details are as follows:

Scheduled Graduation

In order to improve the education of various teams and cultivate cadre talents, the Defense Association specially requested and obtained approval from the Municipal Government to establish a cadre training class. Over 300 students were recommended by various teams throughout the city, and training began on November 3rd of last year. It has been five months since then. It was originally scheduled to graduate after seventeen weeks, a total of four months. However, due to holidays and absences due to cloudy weather, supplementary lessons were needed, so it was decided to postpone the graduation ceremony to the middle of next month.

Live Firing Exercise

Yesterday, Mr. Wu Chuiying of the association told reporters that the cadre training class is approaching the end of its term, and all the academic courses have been taught in sequence. In order to test whether the students' academic performance is excellent, they specially requested and obtained approval from the Municipal Government, the Songhu Garrison Headquarters, and the Municipal Security Office to hold live firing exercises at the Longhua West Fort today and tomorrow.

Request for Awards

The association believes that the students in the training class are all outstanding members of the Shanghai business community and have always fulfilled their obligations to maintain local security. Therefore, awards will be given to those who excel in academics and other subjects to show encouragement. Yesterday, the association submitted a request to the Municipal Government and the Songhu Garrison Headquarters for awards and requested them to attend the graduation ceremony and deliver speeches.

Continued Training

Shanghai is a place where Chinese and foreigners live together, with a vast area and a dense population of good and bad people mixed together. It is very important for the defense team members to assist in maintaining local security. Therefore, in order to popularize self-defense education among various teams, the association decided to continue the second phase of training after the graduation of the first phase of the cadre training class. The number of trainees will remain the same as originally stipulated, but improvements will be made to achieve greater progress.
