Art Exhibition, Preview on the Thirteenth Day 134

Yesterday (the 20th) was the thirteenth day of the Shanghai preview of the International Exhibition of Chinese Art in London. Because the weather was fine and it was Saturday, the number of visitors was even more crowded, and the scene was unprecedented in the past few days. It is estimated that the Shanghai Municipal Education Bureau issued group tickets for over a thousand people yesterday, and several hundred people from Jinan University also came to visit. Together with visitors from other circles, the number reached three thousand. The number of people outside requesting to purchase tickets to enter was even more constant. However, in order to maintain order at the venue, the association limited the number of visitors each day to no more than three thousand. Therefore, those who want to visit the association should purchase tickets early to avoid disappointment. The date of shipping the antiques to England has been set for May 28th. The association is currently working overtime to rush the construction of boxes and prepare customs clearance procedures. The preview will be closed on the 30th of this month. After the closing, the antiques will be packed in boxes. This packing procedure is complicated and will take two weeks to complete. The first chapter of the explanation of the calligraphy and painting compiled by the association, the general outline, has been published in yesterday's newspaper. Now, the third chapter of the explanation, "The Evolution of Calligraphy and Its Famous Masters," is recorded below. By reading this, the situation of Chinese calligraphy can be understood.

The Evolution of Calligraphy and Its Famous Masters

Calligraphy is a kind of Chinese art. Its development can be divided into five periods. From the Shang and Zhou Dynasties to the Qin Dynasty, characters that contained pictographic elements evolved into the Great Seal Script and the Small Seal Script. This is the first period. Many of the characters from this period that have survived, such as those on bronzes and stone carvings, can still be studied. At the end of the Qin Dynasty, the Eight-Part Script was created, and during the Han Dynasty, the Clerical Script, the Cursive Script, and the Wild Cursive Script were created. Zhong Yao of the Wei Dynasty and Wang Xizhi of the Jin Dynasty were famous for their running script and standard script, which are today's styles of calligraphy. Their authentic works still exist in the world, and they became the great masters of today's style of calligraphy. Calligraphers of all dynasties could not surpass their scope until the end of the Six Dynasties. During this period, the Northern Dynasties formed a slightly different school (such as Zheng Xi, etc.), which was majestic, upright, and neat, with its own characteristics. This is the second period. By the Sui Dynasty, the North and the South merged, thus opening the prelude to the Tang Dynasty. Emperor Taizong of the Tang Dynasty, Ouyang Xun, Chu Suiliang, Xue Ji, Lu Jianzhi, Sun Qianli, Zhang Xu, Yan Zhenqing, Huai Su, Liu Gongquan, Li Yong, and Xu Hao each had their own expertise and established their own schools. Literati such as Li Bai, Lin Zao, and Du Mu were all known for their calligraphy. Yang Ningshi of the Five Dynasties integrated various schools and can be called a rising force. This is the third period of calligraphy. Huang Tingjian and Mi Fu continued Yang's efforts and opened the Song Dynasty's special school of calligraphy with four great masters. Later, Emperor Huizong advocated the Slender Gold Script. Emperor Gaozong spent twenty years in Deshou Palace, concentrating on the calligraphy of the Wang brothers. Therefore, literati such as Cai Jing, Zhou Bangyan, Fan Chengda, Zhang Xiaoxiang, Jiang Kui, Lu You, Wu Ju, Wu Shuo, Zhu Xi, and Yue Ke were all famous for their calligraphy. The Liao and Jin people entered China, and culturally, they were assimilated by China. Therefore, Ren Xunwang Tingyun of the Jin Dynasty and Zhao Mengfu of the Yuan Dynasty rose rapidly. Zhao Mengfu was proficient in both calligraphy and painting and can be called the great master of this period. In addition, Xian Yushu, Kangli Shankuai, Yu Ji, Zhang Yu, Jie Xisi, and Yu He of the Yuan Dynasty also had their own unique characteristics. This is the fourth period. The Ming Dynasty inherited the legacy of the Yuan Dynasty. Calligraphers such as Song Ke, Song Lian, Li Dongyang, Zhu Yunming, Wen Zhengming, and Wang Chong all had their own expertise. Dong Qichang later integrated all the styles and was also proficient in both calligraphy and painting. At the beginning of the Qing Dynasty, most of the calligraphers were influenced by him. Wang Duo, Wang Shizhen, Jiang Chenying, Jin Nong, Wang Shu, Liu Yong, Weng Fanggang, and Yi Bingshou were relatively outstanding. After the Jiaqing period, people were tired of the lifelessness of the Pavilion Style and turned to learning the style of stele inscriptions, which changed the calligraphy style. Calligraphy was slightly revitalized, and Deng Shiru and Bao Shichen were representatives of this style. This is the fifth period. (The evolution of calligraphy and its famous masters will be continued tomorrow.)

China Merchants Steam Navigation Company's Nanyang Route Is Still Difficult to Extend to Singapore 136

The Shanghai Chamber of Commerce petitioned the Ministry of Transportation to extend the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company's Hong Kong route to Singapore. The Ministry of Transportation ordered the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company to reply. The company replied that the company has 26 ships, including its own ships and rented ships, which are operating in various ports in Jiangsu and Zhejiang, and they are still not enough to allocate. Moreover, they are not suitable for long-distance ocean voyages. The recently built Hai Yuan, Hai Heng, Hai Li, and Hai Zhen are all four ships, because they are dedicated to domestic navigation needs, so their tonnage and manufacturing are also suitable for the business of coastal ports, and it is really inconvenient to navigate to Singapore. As for the development of the Nanyang route, although the company has considered planning, it has not been realized due to the current economic inability to increase the tonnage. The various points requested by the Singapore Chinese Chamber of Commerce are actually difficult to implement. As for the exhibits of the association, they can only be transported by the company's original domestic routes to Hong Kong. In the future, the freight rate can be reduced with reference to the past exhibition transport precedents to show distinction. Organization of Shipping Cooperative - Directors to be Elected First 142

The shipping cooperative, which is a disguised form of business control, has been in preparation for a year by 21 representatives from state-run and private airlines in the port. After a long period of meetings and investigations by various expert committees, the draft cooperative plan and organizational law have finally been agreed upon and submitted to the ministry. An approval order has now been received, and the cooperative has taken a further step, holding four consecutive meetings to formally establish the cooperative. After public discussion by the representatives, it is planned that the China Shipping Cooperative will be formally established on June 1st, and the joint business offices of each airline will also be established at the same time. The board of directors, the highest authority of the cooperative, should also be established first. The preparatory committee has submitted this to the Shanghai Shipping Association for discussion, and it has been decided that an election of the 11 directors of the cooperative should be held first. The association has resolved to convene a general meeting of all members of the Shanghai Shipping Association on the 29th of this month to hold a vote to elect the directors of the cooperative, stipulating that state-run companies will occupy five seats and private companies will occupy six seats.

Municipal Bureau of Weights and Measures - Preparing for a General Inspection of All Households in the City - Inspection of the Chinese and Rental Areas Has Already Begun This Year - Public Security Bureau and Others Assist, Focusing on Shops and Vegetable Markets 150

The first general inspection of this year by the Municipal Social Bureau's Bureau of Weights and Measures has already begun, starting with the Chinese area, focusing on shops, vegetable markets, and rural towns, while actively promoting a general inspection of more than one million households throughout the city, which is also planned to be carried out. The following is a report from a reporter of the Dagong News Agency on the various situations:

Focus of General Inspection: Shops and Vegetable Markets

Since the authorities urged citizens to actively promote the new system of weights and measures, it has been implemented in both the Chinese and French areas. However, the concession area has not yet been properly negotiated, so no inspection has been carried out. The Municipal Bureau of Weights and Measures is deeply concerned that a small number of citizens may be outwardly compliant but inwardly resistant, and has specifically stipulated that a general inspection will be carried out twice a year. The first general inspection this year has already begun, and the public security bureaus and district police officers of the respective jurisdictions will assist in the handling. The inspection will focus on shops and small vegetable markets. If it is found that a shop has privately manufactured or used weights and measures, the weights and measures will be confiscated, and the shop name and the shopkeeper's name will be reported to the Social Bureau for referral to the court for punishment. In the small vegetable markets, inspectors will carry weights to verify the instruments at any time. If any discrepancies are found, they will be destroyed on the spot to show a warning. After the general inspection of the Chinese area is completed, the police will be convened to inspect various districts of the French Concession.

Active Promotion in Rural Towns and Villages

In various rural towns and villages near this city, such as Pudong Mitsubishi Pond, Yangjing Town, Laolonghua in the western district of Shanghai, Xinlonghua, Caohejing, and Zhabei District, Jiangwan District, Pusong District, Wusong District, Pengpei District, etc., personnel are actively dispatched to promote, follow up on the publicity and urge reform and implementation, so that farmers understand the needs and benefits of the new system of weights and measures, and gradually expect to automatically abandon the old system, in order to achieve practical results, and then start the inspection.

Planned Inspection of All Households in the City

Regarding the work of inspecting the weights and measures of all households in the city, Director Zhou said yesterday that this city is a major commercial port in the country, densely populated, with a total of more than one million households. If the inspection period is uninterrupted every day, it will take a year. However, promoting the new system is the responsibility of the government, and we will actively proceed without any difficulties. We are now drafting plans and procedures, and after approval from the competent authority, we will send all inspectors to set off in different districts and implement a general inspection of households.

Major Fire in Zhabei Last Night - More Than a Hundred Thatched Houses Reduced to Ashes - Fire Engines from All Districts Fully Mobilized 153

No. 269 Changan Road, Zhabei, is a glass bottle old goods store, opened by Wu Changshan from Jiangbei. The house is a flat-roofed house covered with lead sheets. The back house is inhabited by the Wang family, the second landlord. At around 8:10 last night, a fire suddenly broke out in the house inhabited by the Wang family. At that time, Wu Changshan, his wife Yang, and another tenant, Yuan Yan, had gone out to attend a lottery party. When the Wang family saw the cause of the trouble, they could not put it out and immediately ran away. Therefore, by the time the outside noticed, the fire had become uncontrollable. At the same time, the back of the city house was still a thatched house, totaling no less than a hundred or so. In addition, the southeast wind was strong last night, so the fire spread to the left, right, and rear of the house in no time. The fire was so bright that it could not be approached. For a while, the noise was deafening, and the order was in chaos. People helped the old and carried the young, scrambling to run away. Fortunately, the Xinzha Patrol Station was nearby. After discovering the fire, they immediately notified the fire brigade to send fire engines to the scene to put out the fire. At the same time, a full team of armed police officers and the city security team were dispatched to assist in maintaining order. However, the fire was raging at this time, so the water sprayed by the fire engines was not very effective. All the thatched houses in the area were lined up vertically and horizontally, making rescue even more difficult. In the blink of an eye, it turned into a fire pit. The firefighters saw that the fire engines from all four sections of Zhabei were still not enough, so they notified the fire brigades of the Nanshi districts and Dongjiadu to drive fire engines to assist in putting out the fire. After the firefighters worked hard and bravely, they managed to prevent the fire from spreading further. However, the area affected by the disaster was already very vast. It is estimated that from Changan Road, north to the back of Linxiangli on Hengtong Road, east to Linfengli on Huasheng Road, and west to the thatched houses around Tong'anli on Huasheng Road, more than a hundred houses, as well as the Cuiyuan Lumber Store and the pine stack on Changan Road, were destroyed by the fire. The fire was slightly extinguished until about 11:00, but flames still broke out from time to time, and the smell was offensive. The firefighters continued to dispatch fire engines to spray water. It was not until midnight at 12:00 that the fire was completely extinguished. In total, more than a hundred thatched houses, four lead-skinned city houses, and one stack were burned down. The loss cannot be estimated for a while. All the general disaster victims were sitting on the street with one mat each, with sad faces and miserable shapes. After the incident, the governing branch bureau, because the fire starter was not found, summoned the three tenants, Wu Changshan, and others to question the cause of the fire. At the same time, the firefighters were afraid that there would be a tragic case of people being burned to death, so they turned over the rubble in different ways. However, as of the time the reporter finished writing, no bodies burned to death had been found, and no population loss incidents had been reported by the disaster victims. According to the observation of the firefighters, it is roughly hoped that they will be spared, which is a great blessing in misfortune.

The Front Car Bumped, the Back Car Ran Over: Jiang Azhuan Dies Tragically 159

Jiang Azhuan, a Wuxi native residing at No. 2, Hewu Lane, Vermon Road, French Concession (named Azhuan because he had a near-death experience in his early years, meaning "returned from death"), was 56 years old and engaged in the ironmongery business. On the morning of the 19th, he went out on business. At noon, around 12:00 PM, while returning home, he was crossing Avenue Joffre (at the intersection of Vermon Road) from south to north in front of No. 148 Avenue Joffre when a car, No. 6256, belonging to Zhou Liying (transliteration, British), a commissioner of the Jianghai Customs, driven by the chauffeur Zhao Longdi (18 years old, local), was traveling east to west on its way back to residence No. 536 West End Avenue. Jiang could not avoid it and was knocked down by the left rear fender of the car. At that moment, another car, No. 1950, driven by a vice-consul of a certain country, Difaer (transliteration), was following closely behind. Unable to brake in time, the wheels ran over Jiang, causing severe injuries. Officer No. 312, stationed nearby, immediately recorded the license plate numbers of both cars and took the injured man to the Avenue Joffre Police Station, from where he was transferred to Guangci Hospital. Due to severe head and internal injuries, treatment was ineffective, and he died at 2:30 PM that afternoon. The hospital notified the police station, which transported the body to the Tongren Fuyuan Mortuary for an autopsy. Yesterday morning, the police station reported to the Second Special District Court Procuratorate. Prosecutor Wang Ren, along with forensic doctor Wei and clerk Peng Xu, arrived at the mortuary at noon to examine the body. They then took their seats in the courtroom. The case-handling Western detective, Henry, and the Chinese detective reported the investigation process. The deceased's nephew, Jiang Jufa, filed the case, requesting to claim the body for burial and seek justice. The official interrogated witness No. 312. The defendants were absent. The official concluded that Jiang Azhuan had indeed died from car accident injuries. The body was released to the family for burial, pending investigation and handling by the police department.

The Troubles of Wealth: Qiu Changsheng Family Inheritance Dispute Leads to Another Lawsuit. Qiu Changsheng's Cousin Hengbao Files a Suit Claiming Encroachment on Ancestral Property, Alleging Four Generations Living Together and Selling Property to Open a Business, Accumulating Considerable Wealth 161

After the death of Qiu Xiaoqing, who started his career in the pigment business and became a wealthy merchant, his family has been involved in inheritance disputes for years, repeatedly filing lawsuits. However, in each lawsuit, Qiu Changsheng, Qiu’s adopted son who inherited the assets, resolved the disputes by providing funds for settlements, without any clear victories or defeats. However, the Qiu family has many members, so as one dispute subsides, another arises, leaving Changsheng in a situation where he is helping one only for another one to fail. Now, his cousin, Qiu Hengbao, has hired a lawyer and filed a criminal self-accusation with the First Special District Court against Changsheng, Changyin (two brothers) and Qiu Qiyuan, QiYu, and Qitai (grandsons of Qiu Weiqing’s brother, Qiu Peisan), accusing them of encroaching on ancestral property.

Criminal Self-accusation requesting that all the defendants be punished according to Article 356 of the Criminal Law. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Zhan Liangce opened a court session to summon and interrogate the parties involved. Only Changsheng, Qiyuan, and the twelve-year-old Qitai appeared as defendants. Qiyu was in Changshu undergoing military training, and Changyin, being under thirteen years old, did not appear. After Judge Zhan clarified the ages, addresses, and occupations of the plaintiffs and defendants who appeared in court, he ordered the plaintiff, Qiu Hengbao, to state the facts of the accusations. He claimed that the Changsheng brothers were his nephews, and the Qiyuan brothers were his grandnephews. They were close relatives who all revered the same ancestor. Weiqing, Peisan, and he were

Paternal Cousins, Weiqing’s father, Qiu Shirong, was his paternal uncle. In the fourteenth year of the Guangxu reign, Shirong and Shixiang jointly sold seven and a half mu of land located in Dashatou to a man named Zhang, and the proceeds were given to Weiqing and Peisan to come to Shanghai and establish the Dechangrun Pigment Store in partnership with Bei Runsheng and Zhao Yuting. At that time, he was not yet born, so he was later told about the sale of the property by his aunt. However, when Weiqing was alive, he frequently distributed the remaining profits from the business, sometimes three thousand or five thousand, etc., and when he died the defendants collectively occupied, no distribution was ever made. His family has lived together for four generations. The ancestral property has never been divided, but the Shanghai residences of Peisan and Weiqing had already been separated. Whenever he came to Shanghai, he

Resided in Weiqing’s home, and so on. When questioned, the defendant Qiu Changsheng stated that Hengbao was his cousin, and there was originally no ancestral property, so the family had not been separated. Dechangrun was established by his father, Weiqing, his uncle, Peisan, and Zhao Yuting, and had no relationship with Yuan Runsheng. The plaintiff had no shares and had never been given dividends. Since there was no ancestral property in his hometown, there was certainly no sale of ancestral property to use the proceeds to start the store. When the plaintiff's lawyer saw that Qiu was denying everything, he presented Qiu's family genealogy, Qiu Weiqing's obituary, and other documents, and stated that Qiu's family had lived under the same roof for four generations, and the family property had not been divided. In the family genealogy

It Would Be Easy To Prove. While Weiqing’s obituary proved that Weiqing’s parents and wife were in their hometown, and were living with the plaintiff, because the pigment industry was not a big business before the European War, and those in this business were not big merchants, they still left their families in their hometown. Since both parties were living together and sharing wealth, the plaintiff should have had the right to acquire shares in Dechangrun, and Qiu Changsheng was Weiqing's adopted son, which was very clear in the obituary. The defendant’s defense attorney also presented a settlement document from 1932 when Qiu Hengbao’s brother, Qiu Hengcai, was involved in a lawsuit with Qiu Changsheng over the family property, stating that there was also a statement in that document that there was no ancestral property whatsoever, and Qiu Hengbao had also

Signed the Document. The court then turned the document over to Qiu Hengbao, and Qiu only admitted to signing the document, but stated that he did not understand the contents because he was not very literate, and that his brother Hengcai had only asked him to sign as a witness so that he could get 80,000 yuan. Judge Zhan interrogated Zhang Yucai, the witness, about the purchase of the land from the Qiu family. According to Zhang, seven mu of land in Dashatou was jointly sold to him by Qiu Shixiang and Shirong, but many years had passed, the deed had long been burned in a fire, and the land had also been submerged. The witnesses in the case have all since died. The court then scheduled a continued hearing for the afternoon of April 27th.

Yu Huogen Admits Strangling His Own Son; Gestures While Confessing; What He Says Is Vividly Described 162

Yu Huogen, a villager from Yu Jiatang in the south of Hongqiao in Shanghai's west, colluded with his daughter-in-law, Chen, to strangle his son, Yu Guanhong (also known as Jilin), with a rope late at night. The District Court, led by Prosecutor Lei Binzhang, has already opened the coffin at the scene, verified that he had been strangled to death while alive, and ordered a proper reburial. This was reported in yesterday's newspaper. It is now known that Yu Huogen had two sons, the elder son, Yu Guanhong (the deceased), and the younger son, Guanming, who both married early. Guanming died of illness the year before last, leaving behind a blind widow. The family's life was quite difficult. In addition, Guanhong became a degenerate and developed addictions. Valuables in the home were stolen by Guanhong and pawned for money. He even stole property from other families. Therefore, the father, who was over sixty years old, hated him to the bone. Although he repeatedly advised him, his bad habits were difficult to change, so he decided to murder his degenerate son to eliminate future troubles. After the case occurred, his daughter-in-law, Yu Chen, was detained by the police and questioned by the court. When the judge arrived at the scene for inspection, Yu Huogen (the perpetrator), the father of the deceased, frankly admitted that he had murdered his son and said that because of his degenerate son's various misdeeds, he did not even consider the consequences and carried out the murder. In the middle of the night on the tenth day of this month, taking advantage of his son's sound sleep, he brought a rope into the room, got on the bed, and put the rope around his son's neck. He was just about to tighten it when his son woke up and resisted. Because he was old and weak, he could not resist, so he quickly called his daughter-in-law to come and help hold down his son's legs. He was able to calmly tighten the rope, and his son quickly died. When Yu Huogen confessed, he gestured vividly, and his description was vivid. The judge originally intended to take him to the court for detention, but Yu Huogen suffered from ascites, with a belly as big as a five-stone gourd, and it was difficult for him to move, so he ordered the local guarantor to take good care of him. However, Yu Chen denied helping to commit the crime. The judge believed that the case was clear and that a public prosecution could be initiated in a few days.

Yesterday (the 20th) was the day of waiting for Jesus' resurrection. Today is the day of Jesus' resurrection. The Catholic Church held a high mass ceremony on all three days. The priests and acolytes are very busy.

Apprentice Falls to His Death from a High Building 168

Shen Zitian, a young man from Chongming, was eighteen years old and was learning the art of bricklaying from Wu Musheng, a local. He was currently working on a new building of the Avenue Edward Military Police Station (behind the original site of the Big Clock) being constructed by Xinlinji Construction Factory under the leadership of Wu. Yesterday morning, Shen was working on the scaffolding outside the ninth floor. At 11:30 AM, Shen went down from the scaffolding to have lunch. He lost his balance and fell from a great height, causing his brains to burst, his right arm to be broken, and his internal organs to be severely damaged. He was barely alive. His master, Wu Mugen, hired a car to send him to Renji Hospital in the Mekajon for treatment. Due to his severe injuries, he died shortly after arriving at the hospital. The Mekajon Police Station was notified and sent officers to transport the body to the Tongren Fuyuan Mortuary for an autopsy, pending the Second Special District Court sending someone to examine the body tomorrow. The deceased's family is still in their hometown, and Wu has sent someone to the countryside to urge them to come to Shanghai to claim the body.

The Dung King's Inheritance Lawsuit Continues: Old Accountant Attends Court Ill, Ordered to Submit Account Books Within Five Days 176

The late Ma Fuqi (also known as Gu Fuqi), the "Dung King" residing on Rue de Villermont in the French Concession, and his wife A Gui Ru, accumulated millions in assets through contracting cleaning services in the British and French concessions and the four districts of Nantao and Zhabei in Japan. They also engaged in rickshaw and real estate businesses. They had three sons: Hongkui (the eldest), Hongsheng (the second), and Honggen (the third). After the deaths of Ma and his wife, all inheritance and business operations were managed by the eldest son, Hongkui. Hongkui also passed away due to illness last autumn, leaving behind his wives, Chen and Wang, and a son and two daughters. Recently, Hongkui's wife, Ma Chen, along with her children, hired a lawyer to file a lawsuit in the Criminal Division of the Special Court against her husband's younger brother, Ma Honggen, her husband's concubine, Ma Wang, and Wan Sanduo, the old accountant who had served for many years, alleging

conspiracy to embezzle public and private inheritance, amounting to four million gold. Judge Qiu Huan Ying of the Special Court has held two hearings and personally visited Wan Sanduo's home to question him (due to Wan being bedridden), where Wan handed over the iron box key and insurance policies. The court ordered a postponement for further hearings and instructed both parties to attempt reconciliation during the adjournment, as detailed in previous reports. Yesterday morning, the third hearing took place. The plaintiff, Ma Chen, and the defendants, Ma Honggen and Ma Wang, each attended with their lawyers. The third defendant, Wan Sanduo, was compelled to attend due to his designation as a defendant. He was seated in a rattan chair, carried to the courthouse by two servants

to await the hearing. At ten o'clock, Judge Qiu, accompanied by court clerk Zhang Guan Cheng, opened the Second Criminal Court for the hearing. After summoning and identifying the parties involved, the judge first questioned Zhu Xuan, the assistant accountant of the Ma family, regarding the rental income from the properties. Zhu testified that he only managed the collection of funds and had no land registers, only property rental forms, with an annual income of approximately 59,000 yuan. He then pointed out the relevant entries in the account books submitted previously. The court then questioned the defendant Ma Honggen about whether reconciliation had been attempted during the adjournment. Ma replied that no reconciliation had been reached due to their lack of sincerity. Ma's defense lawyer then stated in court that Tan Keng Fu and others had contacted Ma Chen regarding the matter, but

the figures presented by the two sides differed too greatly, with one side claiming assets of four million and the other claiming only over ten thousand, leading to no resolution. The plaintiff, Ma Chen, stated that she was willing to reconcile if they turned over the assets, but would not agree to reconciliation if the difference was too great. She asserted that the assets were indeed four million yuan, as she had heard her mother-in-law and husband say before their deaths. The judge then said to Chen, "You are all one family, you should each make concessions, why insist so stubbornly?" The judge then inquired about the deposit in the Ma Hong Ji branch of the Bank of China. Ma Honggen replied that the funds were from his brother Hongsheng's personal business managing the public concession's

garbage and not jointly owned. At this point, the plaintiff's lawyer stated that "Ma Hong Ji" was a shared name, while names like "Hong Ji," "Kui Hong Ji," "Wang Ji," and "Hong Gen Ji" were separate names for each individual. The judge then questioned the second defendant, Ma Wang, about the custody of the seals and keys to the safe and iron box, after which he questioned the third defendant, Wan Sanduo. Wan was still carried to the court by servants. Unable to stand, he was questioned while seated. The judge loudly questioned Wan about the existence of a general ledger of the Ma family's assets and the management of the property rentals. Wan, hard of hearing due to his illness and speaking in a low voice, required a bailiff to relay the questions. Wan replied that the Ma family had no

general land register. He and Wu Zhongming managed a portion of the rent, while Te Back & Co. and the Fair Foreign Company managed the rest. The court then questioned him further about the amount of rent he managed, stating, "You have helped this family for several decades, now that they are in a lawsuit, you should speak from your conscience." Wan replied that there were rent receipts and other evidence that could be checked. He had only taken over as the chief accountant on January 16th of last year. Before that, he merely assisted the old lady, A Gui Jie, in running errands. Later, Hongkui managed the business and consulted with him. He now submitted three reports each month to the three people. When asked about Hongkui's seal, Wan replied that it was still in the iron box. The court then ordered Wan to submit the account books and property lists from 1915 within five days, and instructed both parties to jointly engage accountants to liquidate the assets. The case was adjourned to be heard again at a later date and the court was dismissed.

Sports News

Li Huitang and Bao Jiaping Take on Difficult Roles: South China Secures Special Silver Shield, Defeats Police Team 2-1 177

Hong Kong News: The annual Special Silver Shield football competition, established in 1897, has been held for 35 sessions. The Royal Navy and Marines Football Team has the best overall record, with South China having won the championship three times. This year's 36th edition, after weeks of intense competition, resulted in South China and the Western Police teams reaching the final. The final match was held at the Hong Kong Football Club ground at 4:15 PM on Saturday, the 13th. Knowing that the Western Police team was strong defensively, South China asked the "Football King" Li Huitang and the "Iron Hand" Bao Jiaping to take on extremely difficult roles to enhance their attacking power and defense. The two, feeling they could not refuse the call of duty, selflessly agreed. As a result, South China's strength surged, attracting the attention of football fans. An endless stream of people spared time to attend the match, and the vast Hong Kong Football Club ground was instantly packed, a rare sight in recent times. As a result of the match, the heavenly star's destiny came true, and the holy water general's sudden kick secured South China's fame, winning this year's championship with a score of 2-1, earning them a place in the annals of history.

Bao Jiaping's Contribution is Greatest

Before describing the battle, this reporter will attempt to assess the performances of both sides. South China's victory was hard-earned, and the greatest contribution came from Bao Jiaping. His saves of dangerous shots were beyond the abilities of others. He certainly earned applause, and I say that South China's victory is owed to Bao's efforts. Second to him were Li Gan and Lin Depu, with Yang Benhan also performing well. "Football King" Li Huitang showed his brilliance once again, but because he had been away from practice for so long, he was not as agile as in the past, but his strength remained. As for the Western Police team, their forwards were mediocre and repeatedly missed opportunities, especially Ji Lian. Di Pai Lu and Morse were still active, but because the midfielders' shots were inaccurate, they were not outstanding. On the defensive end, Pak Kin Shi's saves of dangerous shots, Parker Spiro's clearances, and Goff Brooks' defensive and offensive support were actually better than South China's. The reason why South China was able to frequently penetrate the Western Police's defense was because the Western Police team was intimidated by Li Huitang's reputation. In addition to using Goff to defend him, they also had Brooks assist. Parker continued to defend Yang Shuiyi closely, so their left side and center were very solid, but this shifted the weakness to the right side, where only Blakeburn defended Li Shiyou. Blakeburn, as a defender, dared not go too far forward, nor too far back, which is why Li Shiyou was more active than Yang Shuiyi. South China was thus able to take the opportunity to attack, and the Western Police team could not help but find themselves in danger. The two goals they conceded were both impossible to save, so South China's victory was not accidental. The details of the performance are recorded below:

First Half: No Winner

After both sides arranged their formations, South China immediately kicked off and attacked. Before reaching the midfield line, the ball was intercepted and the Western Police launched a counterattack with great momentum, advancing to South China's goal, but were unable to shoot. Li Gan stole the ball and sent it forward. Li Huitang advanced to the Western Police's back line, but lost an opportunity due to slowness. Li Shiyou then attacked again, getting an opportunity to cross the ball. The ball passed in front of the goal, but Li Zhaorong was unable to meet it in time, missing another opportunity. Parker cleared the ball and assisted the forwards in attacking. Brooks took a long shot, which Bao Jiaping caught with one hand, finally clearing the danger. Li Huitang received the ball and counterattacked, with Li Zhaorong assisting him. They forced a corner kick. Yang Shuiyi kicked it in well. Li Huitang responded with a shot, but unfortunately it missed the mark. At this point, the two sides had been fighting for over twenty minutes, but had not yet opened the scoring. Later, the Western Police team made a stunning move. Di Pai Lu broke through from the side and took a quick shot. Although Bao Jiaping caught it, it still resulted in a corner kick. Di Pai Lu kicked it in well. Stephens kicked it high and away. The Western Police's attack failed, and Li Shiyou seized the opportunity, making a long drive and dribbling past Blakeburn to cross the ball. Pak Kin Shi pounced to save it. The ball rolled back to Li Shiyou's feet. Li kicked it, but Xin Shipi was alert and stood in the goal. Seeing the ball coming, he knelt to save it and clear the danger, ensuring that the defense was not breached. Working together as brothers, Di Pai Lu

counterattacked and won another corner kick, but failed to capitalize on it. However, South China

was surrounded for a while. Fortunately, Yang Benhan returned to the rescue, breaking through the encirclement and sending the ball to Li Shiyou for an attack, resulting in a corner kick, but it was saved by Parker. South China then retreated. Western Police team leader Johnston counter-attacked, and South China was in imminent danger. Parker released a cold arrow, which Bao Jiaping hastily slapped away, averting the crisis. Ji Xiao continued to be active, passing to Johnston, who headed the ball out of bounds. South China was in danger again. Before one wave subsided, another rose. The Western Police's three forwards surged forward. Although Bao Jiaping caught the ball, he was forced to concede a corner kick due to the danger. Although the Western Police gained this advantage, they did not get anything out of it. After this, both sides attacked and defended, each with its own dangers, but the result remained the same, with no opening score. The first half ended in a 0-0 draw.

2-1: Winning the Championship

After a ten-minute break, the exhausted troops resumed the battle. The Western Police pressed forward with renewed vigor, but were repelled by Yu Qingyuan and Yang Benhan. The Western Police surged forward like a tide, retreating and advancing in turn. South China, unprepared for this, had their defense breached by Brooks, who sent the ball forward. Only four minutes had passed since the first goal. South China, having taken a 2-0 lead, still did not slacken. Seeing that the situation was dire, the Western Police adopted a scorched earth strategy. Spiro was switched to the left wing to increase their attacking power. Sure enough, under a desperate effort, they gained the upper hand and surrounded South China several times. Johnston and Stephens shot, but were both saved by Bao Jiaping. South China also attempted several counterattacks, but without success. The Western Police continued their attack and, in the final minute of the match, Ji Lian, taking advantage of Di Pai Lu's cross, headed the ball back, making the score 2-1, and the game ended. Eleventh Day of the Reading Movement; He Bingsong Lectures on the Study of History and Geography 190

Yesterday was the eleventh day of the National Reading Movement Conference organized by the China Cultural Construction Association. They specially invited the history and geography expert He Bingsong to lecture on how to study history and geography. The full text of the record is as follows: Today, I am honored by the kindness of the China Cultural Construction Association to have me speak to you about how to study history and geography. I will now present my humble opinions and discuss them with you, and I ask for your guidance.

The Nature of History and Geography

We will now first discuss the nature of the two sciences, history and geography. History is the science that studies the past lives and activities of mankind. Geography is the science that studies the present lives and activities of mankind. The objects of these two sciences are generally the same. However, the study of history takes time as its warp, which means we want to study the course of human life and activities from the most ancient times up to the present. However, human life and activities cannot be separated from the earth, so we cannot but take the study of geography, which studies space, as the weft. As for the study of geography, it takes the surface of the earth as its warp, so the surface of the earth, including the strata below and the atmosphere above, is what we want to study: how humans conquer and utilize the surface of this earth to improve their lives and promote cultural activities. However, humans conquering and utilizing the surface of the earth cannot be accomplished in a single day, so we cannot but take history as the weft. In this way, although history and geography are, one, the study of humans in time, and the other, the study of humans in space, because what they study are human life and activities, they have the effect of being mutually useful and cannot be neglected.

The Object of Study in History and Geography

The so-called life and activities of mankind can generally be divided into five types: political, economic, religious, educational, and artistic. These five types of life and activities form what is called human culture. When we study the history of mankind or of various countries, we take their culture as our object, that is, these five types of life and activities as our object. The same is true for geography. However, because what geography studies, in addition to the above five types of life and activities, also pays special attention to the problem of mankind conquering the surface of the earth, therefore, when we study geography, we also have to simultaneously study the area, natural resources, climate, land and water transportation, etc. of the entire earth or of various countries to see how they affect human life and activities. This is what is commonly called human geography. Recently, some people have said that a history of human culture is the history of mankind conquering and utilizing nature. What is called nature is the object of geography. Then we can also say that history is past human geography, and geography is modern cultural history. Simply put, the object of history is the past culture of mankind, and the object of geography is the culture that mankind continues to create on the surface of the earth in modern times.

Purpose and Value

Our purpose in studying history and geography, like that of other sciences, lies in seeking truth. What is called truth, in history, is the truth of the various lives and activities of mankind in the past in culture, and in geography, is the truth of the various lives and activities of mankind in the present in culture. We want to understand the truth of mankind's past culture to help us determine the path to fight for culture, so that we will not go down the wrong path again. We want to understand the truth of mankind's present culture to serve as a reference for us to create a new culture. Arriving at the usefulness of knowing oneself and knowing one's enemy, I think that this is perhaps the purpose and value of the two sciences of history and geography, and the reason why we should study these two sciences.

The Importance of Seeking Truth

Why do the purposes of history and geography both require seeking truth? This is because truth is originally the highest ideal of mankind. All conclusions that are deliberately false, or that only see a part, do not conform to the spirit of science, and we should all reject them. In studying history and geography, in particular, it is not appropriate to have subjective opinions, or to reverse right and wrong, or to confuse black and white, or to generalize from the particular. Studying history and geography with this kind of view is like wearing a pair of colored glasses to observe everything in front of us. The colors we see are only for our own appreciation, and the conclusions we reach are also only colored conclusions. It is okay to take them to promote personal claims, but if they are regarded as a contribution to science, there is a big problem. This attitude problem is very important, and we who study history and geography must be vigilant at all times to prevent it.

Methods of Studying History and Geography

Since the purpose of studying history and geography is to seek the truth, then we can only adopt the modern so-called scientific method. The characteristics of the scientific method are: first, our attitude must be able to be absolutely objective. When we study history and geography, we must absolutely eliminate our own prejudices, and restore the original appearance of right and wrong. "To know is to know, to not know is to not know," and we must absolutely not add or subtract anything, or only see one part, or only see the majority, we must absolutely not claim to have seen the whole. Then, the characters and events of history, and the people and customs of various places in the modern world, can raise their heads and reveal their true faces, otherwise they will all be hidden in the thick fog of our prejudices. This is the first characteristic of the scientific method, which is an objective attitude. The second is that we should apply observation methods. This method is undoubtedly applicable to geographical research, because we now have many scientific machines and instruments to help us work. For example, to measure the atmosphere and the height of mountains, we can use balloons, airplanes, or airships. To measure the depth and breadth of the ocean and the earth's strata, we can use ships and explosives. To measure the shape of the ground, we can use airplanes. The natural state of the earth today, except for the polar regions because of the cold climate, which still need our efforts, has almost been observed clearly. As for the modern human cultural part, there are also statistics from various governments for reference, and there are also generally ways to deal with it.

Historical Research Methods

Only history, because the past is all past, there is of course no way to observe it. There are not many ancient relics left to the present, and they cannot be regarded as the entire reference. Therefore, we can only rely on the records of the ancients to be our basis. Therefore, this science of history cannot be regarded as a pure science. However, there is another modern method of studying history, which is the textual research method of historical materials that our people say. The so-called historical materials include relics and written records as the main components. There are two most important principles for textual research of historical materials. First, the most historical materials are required to be as complete as possible, so-called complete without omission. Second, the truth obtained in the most extensive historical materials, or the truth sought without an objective attitude, is not the scientific truth in history, and we must absolutely not trust it. Therefore, we must both demand the most extensive historical materials and use the most objective attitude to conduct textual research on them to seek the truth. The work of textual research of historical materials can be divided into two steps. The first step is to conduct textual research on whether the author of the historical materials is an honest, trustworthy, cautious, and unbiased person. This is the so-called effort of "knowing the world and knowing the person." The second step is to conduct textual research on whether this historical material is an original or a fake made by later generations. This is the so-called effort of "textual research of authenticity." Every historical material must go through this effort. Only when the author of the historical material and the historical material itself are reliable can we trust him and regard the situation he recorded as the truth of a certain ancient person or a certain major event. This kind of textual research effort is the most important step in studying history. Because of time constraints, we cannot talk more about it. If you are interested, please read my book "Historical Research Methods," which can give you a general idea. And about how we apply the method of induction to synthesize the facts recorded in the historical materials to seek the truth, and how we apply the method of deduction to infer the general outline of the truth from the facts recorded in a part of the historical materials, I think this is something that everyone who understands the art of thinking and textual research already knows, so I don't need to go into detail. Third, in the scientific method, there is also the so-called experiment, which cannot be applied in history, because the people and events of the past cannot be revived and reappear for us to experiment on again and again. In geography, we can only apply the method of verification to confirm the observations of others, but it is much more convenient and accurate than history.

Conclusion

In short, if we want to understand the past and present culture of mankind, we should study a little history and geography. When we study history and geography, we should maintain an objective attitude and make full use of scientific methods to seek the truth of various lives and activities of mankind in culture. We must never reverse right and wrong, nor can we turn falsehood into truth. We must write straight and tell the truth without concealing anything. This is perhaps the lesson that the study of history and geography gives us. The end.

Luoyang Promotes Compulsory Free Education 194

(Luoyang, 20th dispatch) Luoyang's promotion of compulsory free education is quite strong. All 170,000 students in the county have the opportunity to receive education.

Literacy Education Committee; Literacy Publicity Week Begins on May 1; Detailed Plan Passed at Yesterday's Publicity Meeting; Divided into Seven Days for Agriculture, Industry, Commerce, Academics, Recreation, and Film 195

The Literacy Education Committee of this city convened a publicity meeting at the Party Headquarters meeting room at 2:00 PM yesterday, inviting representatives from all walks of life to discuss the implementation methods and decided to hold a Literacy Publicity Week starting on May 1. The details are recorded as follows.

Attending Representatives: The total number of attendees included the director-general of the committee, Tao Baichuan, deputy director-general Jiang Jianbai, Huang Xianggu from the Municipal Party Headquarters, Zhang Yuanruo from the Municipal Government, Lv Hailan and Li Wanyu from the Municipal Education Bureau, Li Kuai and Li Guangteng from the Municipal Education Association, Zhu Zumo from the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, Yu Zhenhui from the Municipal Farmers' Association, Shao Xubai from the General Labor Union, Lin Kecong from the Women's Association, Wang Wanbai from the Wireless Broadcasting Association, Wei Yuqing and Zhou Yinfan from Guangyu Society, Chen Binru from Runyu Society, etc. Tao Baichuan presided over the meeting, and Lu Haishan recorded the proceedings. After the rituals, the chairman first reported, and then the publicity plan was passed as follows.

Publicity Goals: (1) To make the public aware that the literacy education movement being promoted by this committee is not a simple literacy education, but a national salvation movement that combines literacy education, common sense guidance, and civic training; (2) To make the public aware that the methods of promoting literacy education by this committee are divided into two types: one is remedial classes in schools, and the other is remedial classes outside schools. Under the first method, this committee will establish hundreds of literacy schools starting on July 1, forcing out-of-school people to go to school in batches for one hour a day, for a period of two months. Under the second method, this committee has requested the Shanghai Party and government agencies to stipulate by order that all Party members, civil servants, and school teachers and students have the obligation to teach people to read. Out-of-school people who have real difficulties in attending school are allowed to find their own teachers, or the committee will introduce the above-mentioned personnel to serve as teachers, receive textbooks, and study at home, and wait for the committee to convene tests after a certain period of time; (3) To make the public aware that it is necessary to start with investigation to handle this literacy education, so this committee will dispatch a large number of investigators between May and June to conduct door-to-door investigations of out-of-school people, so that they can be taught according to their aptitude in the future; (4) To make the public aware that this literacy movement is not only important, but also difficult, and compounded by the fact that this committee has few personnel and limited capabilities, it cannot be done without the assistance of all sectors of society. If they can widely publicize it verbally and give good guidance, the committee is already very grateful; (5) To create a warm and strong reading atmosphere, at least to make the public aware that this city is about to force out-of-school people to receive literacy education.

Publicity Plan: The ten experimental schools of this committee's Jiangwan District are scheduled to open on May 1, and the twenty-two district offices are also scheduled to be officially established on this day. The investigation of out-of-school people in various districts is scheduled to begin on the 8th, so these seven days are designated as Publicity Week, and their order is as follows: (1) Industry Publicity Day: (A) Hold the opening ceremony of the Shanghai Literacy Movement Week, and at the same time, the district offices are established, and the inauguration ceremony of the district directors and chairmen of the district investigation committees is held jointly; (B) This day happens to be May 1st Labor Day, it is planned to contact the General Labor Union to expand publicity, so that workers know the meaning of the May 1st Festival, in fighting for the three-eight system, and the three-eight system has eight hours of education in addition to eight hours of work and eight hours of rest; (C) The Jiangwan experimental schools hold an opening ceremony; (D) Major daily newspapers and tabloids each write a literacy education commentary; (E) Major daily newspapers compile and print a half-page special edition on the literacy movement, and the materials are provided by the committee; (F) Please add this committee's specially made slides to be shown in each movie theater for seven consecutive days; (2) Radio Publicity Day: (A) Urge popular education experts to give radio lectures; (B) Mobilize all radio stations' broadcasting and entertainment personnel to compile and broadcast literacy movement materials; (C) The committee compiles a simple description of the literacy movement and asks each radio station to report it; (3) Business Publicity Day: (A) Ask the Municipal Chamber of Commerce to issue a letter to merchants for the literacy movement; (B) Ask the Municipal Chamber of Commerce to notify each store to post slogans uniformly; (4) Entertainment Publicity Day: (A) Mobilize the entertainment personnel of all stages and entertainment venues, whether it is duets, storytelling, acrobatics, etc., please intersperse literacy movement materials; (B) This committee holds a costume lecture in Nanshi; (C) This committee sends personnel to each stage to give lectures; (D) Go to each entertainment venue to distribute leaflets and post slogans; (5) Film Publicity Day: (A) Contact the Film Education Association to choose a location to show educational films; (B) Select films with rich literacy education significance to screen at a chosen location on this morning, and invite the general public who are illiterate to watch for free; (6) Academic Publicity Day: (A) This day happens to be Monday, please ask the school authorities to lecture on the promotion of literacy education during the weekly memorial service; (B) Print leaflets with pictures and ask elementary and middle school students to take them home and persuade out-of-school people to read; (C) Please ask the Education Bureau to issue a notice to each school to organize publicity teams as appropriate and go out to promote publicity during after-school hours; (7) Agricultural Publicity Day: (A) This committee's twenty-two district offices, together with the district farmers' associations, widely promote publicity in rural areas; (B) Please ask the Municipal Farmers' Association to issue a letter to farmers for the literacy movement; (C) Airplanes go to the countryside to distribute leaflets.

Spring and Autumn Children's Weekly

How to Be a "Scientific Child"? 197

— Jun Peng

Children! We must know that the world today is a scientific world. Within this scientific world, there must be a "scientific China." Who will create this scientific China? We, the children of today! But how do we become "scientific children"?

Hand-Brain Alliance: Science emerges from playing with tricks. These scientific tricks cannot be played blindly. If you only know how to play and don't think, then you're only fit to be a lackey under the "King of Tricks," not a "scientific child." Don't forget these two readily available VIPs: "Hands and Brain." You must ask the brain to be the commander-in-chief and the hands to be ten little soldiers. Everyone must form an alliance and attack all the mysteries in the universe.

Two Detectives: You can't attack nature without detectives. Children! Can you guess who they are? One is called the eye, and the other is called the ear. Your eyes are originally bright, so why are you wearing tinted glasses? Take off the tinted glasses, and they become your all-seeing eyes. Your ears are originally able to hear clearly, so why are you wearing superstitious earmuffs? Take them off, and they become your all-hearing ears. With all-seeing eyes and all-hearing ears as detectives, your commander-in-chief, two generals, and ten little soldiers will be able to know yourself and know your enemy, and win every battle.

Living Military Books: Fighting requires military books, otherwise you'll have courage without strategy. But these are living books—wind, rain, clouds, snow, sun, moon, stars, and all the transformations in the universe. These are all living books. When the sky thunders, you must ask, "What is the reason for that?" During solar and lunar eclipses, your two detectives must not be fooled. If they say, "A lunar eclipse is a wild moon eating a domestic moon," would you believe it? Ah! To seek true knowledge, you must first unravel all such mysteries in the natural world, and use these living books on this great battlefield.

Literary Stories 198

— Sun Yucai, Xu Zhengji

(1) Painting Reeds to Teach Her Son

During the Song Dynasty, there was a scholar named Ouyang Xiu. When he was only four years old, his father died. At that time, the family was very poor. His mother, Zheng, couldn't afford paper and ink, so she used reeds (a type of rush) to draw on the ground to teach him how to read and write.

Through his mother's teaching, Ouyang Xiu's intelligence was greatly developed, and he gradually achieved considerable success in his studies.

Later, under the guidance of a good teacher, he passed the imperial examination and became an official. He indeed made some contributions during the Song Dynasty and was later known as Layman of the Sixth One. He wrote many books, including the New Book of Tang and the New History of the Five Dynasties, which are very famous.

Zong Que's Childhood Ambition

When Zong Que was very young, he was able to study hard. One day, his uncle, Shao Wen, called him over and asked, "What is your ambition for the future?" Zong Que said, "My ambition for the future is to ride the long winds and break through the waves for thousands of miles!" His uncle was very impressed. Later, Zong Que indeed became a famous general of his time, received the order to conquer Lin Yi, and was granted the title of Marquis of Taoyang.

Watering Flowers and Eating 199

— Da Zhai

Since I was young, I have liked flowers, and I especially like growing them myself. Although it takes some effort to cultivate them, I didn't understand the proper watering methods at first. I thought that to love flowers, I had to water them more often, the more times I watered them each day, the better. Little did I know that it was counterproductive, doing more harm than good. The flowers that were overwatered became weak. Later, I learned that watering flowers must be done at set times and according to standards.

Flowers absorb water for nourishment, and people's nourishment comes from eating. People's eating is just like watering flowers: it must be done at set times and according to standards. If you eat snacks excessively outside of mealtimes, it will invisibly damage your spleen and stomach, harm your nutrition, and hinder your health, just as the saying goes, "Eating without benefiting." I see some children—especially those from families with ample means—who eat a lot of snacks before lunch. When it's time for lunch, even though there are delicious dishes laid out, they don't seem appetizing to them. They can only eat a few bites before putting down their chopsticks. The mothers, who don't understand the reason and are overly doting, always say, "This child is so strange! How can he not eat when there are such good dishes?" In fact, they are too full from snacking before meals. Being full leads to a dislike of meals. It's not that the dishes don't taste good or that the appetite is too small. As the ancients said, "Strive to eat more rice." If you can't strive to eat rice, then you will naturally lack nutrition, resulting in thin muscles or even a pale complexion. This bad habit greatly affects your physique. You should know that building up your physique is very important, just like how well-nourished flowers will naturally flourish!

Pencils Also Use Inkwells Now 200

— Yi An

Flying Kites Can Release Internal Heat 201

— Xing Xia

All lively children love to fly kites in the spring. This is because it's a manifestation of the season, because they have beautiful colors and soaring postures, and because they can induce natural movement. At the same time, it can also provide a change of fresh air. This highly beneficial entertainment is truly of great benefit to children. It is said that, in addition to the above benefits, it can also allow children to release internal heat. As stated in the "Supplement to the Record of Diverse Matters," "Today's kites are raised by strings, causing children to open their mouths and look up, in order to release internal heat." This saying is quite correct. Originally, those suffering from eye diseases and poor health signs (such as eye problems, choking coughs, fever...) are due to having too much internal heat in the spring compared to the other three seasons. That is, "spring has more internal heat." Now, unknowingly releasing internal heat by playing with kites is certainly extremely good. However, again, there's something else to remember. While releasing internal heat is certainly a benefit of kites, children who love to play with kites must also remember one thing: always fly kites with your back to the wind and looking up. If you must open your mouth and look up as mentioned above, be sure to do so in a place with fresh air. Do not run against the wind to avoid stomach wind and causing much concern for your parents.

Owl 202

— Wen Yuyang

Children! I'll teach you how to make an owl toy. It's a very fun toy. First, prepare the following materials (as shown in the picture): one nail, two bamboo sticks, three round pieces of paper, four, five, and six pieces of wood, seven pine cones and half a pine cone. The size of each material should be based on the pine cone as the standard. After you have prepared all the materials, first hammer the nail in the middle of the wood, as in (Figure 1). Then nail the four, five, and six pieces of wood together to form a T-shape, as in (Figure 2). Draw a pair of eyes on the two pieces of paper, as in (Figure 3). Stick them on top of the half pine cone. Insert a bamboo stick below the eyes to make a mouth. Then insert two bamboo sticks at the end of the pine cone to make feet. Put the half pine cone on top, and you have an owl toy!

— Zhen

Spring is good, happiness arrives.

Giggling and laughing, flying a kite.

Older brother holds the kite,

Younger brother winds the string;

Together they run straight to the field.

What kind of kite are they flying?

It turns out to be a butterfly kite.

A gust of wind blows,

Busy letting out the string,

Looking up,

It's already in mid-air,

Looks just like a living bird.

Younger brother jumps for joy,

Younger sister stares blankly.

Children's Science Lecture: Fish and Life 205

— Lin Yin

When I talk about fish with children, everyone is excited and will answer, "I love to eat fish!" Many children have also told me that they have seen many kinds of fish. Friends have also written about fish in this magazine. Here, I want to tell children about some interesting aspects of fish life.

Look at the cuttlefish (Figure 1). It has an ink sac in its belly that can produce ink. When it encounters an animal that harms it, it releases ink to make the enemy unable to see it, allowing it to escape. Similar in shape to the cuttlefish is the octopus (Figure 2). It loves beauty and often changes its clothes. It often changes its color according to the weather and the rising and falling of the sun and moon. Sometimes it's pale yellow, sometimes it's moon white, sometimes it's mud gray, and sometimes it's grass green. Think about it, how fun is that! (Figure 3) shows the starfish. It has a special ability. When its body splits, it can still continue its life. If you tear it into fragments and throw it back into the water, after a certain period of time, the torn parts will grow back as before and turn into several starfish. However, if it is torn apart for more than fifteen minutes, its life cannot be sustained. The seahorse (Figure 4) is born very special, and its swimming method is also completely different from other fish. Its head looks like a horse's head, its eyes protrude outward, and it swims with its body upright. Its tail looks like a cat's tail. When the waves crash, it hooks its tail onto rocks or seaweed to avoid danger. (Figure 5) is the croaker. Its pectoral fins are particularly large, like two wings. It has a special skill, which is that it can sing and bark. This is because its swim bladder is very thick. When the two swim bladders touch, contracting and expanding, a "gululi gululi" sound is produced. The sunfish (Figure 6) has a very large body, more than two zhang long and more than 1,500 pounds heavy, like a large chicken heart. Its tail is very powerful, and its strength is also very great. Sea ships are often overturned by it. Because small animals in the sea are afraid of it and avoid it, it often uses the method of pretending to be dead to catch other fish for food.

Children! The lives of fish in the sea are very interesting. You can study them more. These are just a few very common ones.

Paper Living Fish 206

— Feng

I know that when children see a title like mine, they will definitely think it's a hoax. How can a paper fish live? That's right, a paper fish certainly can't live. However, there is a way to make a paper fish flip back and forth, looking as if it's moving like a living fish. Think about it: how interesting would this gadget be!

The method is very easy. Just take a small strip of transparent paper (like glass) and cut it into the shape of a fish according to the attached diagram.

When playing, use half a cup of very hot tea or boiling water. Cover the cup with a piece of paper to prevent the heat from escaping. Then place the fish on the paper, and the paper fish will move continuously.

Excursion Group (Picnic in the lower left corner) 207

— (Photo by Zhang Yian)

Use transparent paper to cut in this way. Place the paper on the bowl, and put the fish on the paper.

The Voyages of Sinbad the Sailor (14) 208

— Xin Qing

One day the king summoned me. When I arrived before him, he said, "Sinbad, I love you. In my heart, I think you should take a wife and live here, and no longer think about your own homeland."

Naturally, I had to do as the king said, so he gave me a wealthy woman from the court as my wife.

I lived in this place for a long time, but although I had great wealth and a noble wife, my life could never make me happy. My great desire was to return once, to see my relatives and friends in the city of Baghdad. My heart was filled with plans on how to see them.

While I was thinking this way, a friend of mine came to see me in great sorrow, because his wife had just died.

I told him that I had heard of his loss and was very upset.

I said, "May God grant you long life."

He said, "Stop! How can you think that I can live long? I don't have many days to live."

I told him not to look at things so pessimistically, and I hoped that he could live for many more years.

Then he told me that there was a strange thing to tell me. I learned from him about the law of this place: when a man dies, his wife must be placed in the grave with him. If a wife dies, her husband must also enter the grave with her body, taking only a jug of water and a few small loaves of bread with him.

When I heard this, I was filled with terror. So I went to ask the king whether this law might apply to me, since I was not born in this place if my wife died. The king told me that when my wife died, I would have to be treated the same way as my poor friend.

He said, "Sinbad, everyone who lives in this place must be treated the same. Even if I am the king, if my queen dies first, I must go with her. So why shouldn't you?"

The day came when my friend's deceased wife was buried in the grave. She was wearing her best clothes and adorned with precious jewels. They carried her body to the top of a high mountain. There was a deep mine shaft there, with a large stone covering the opening.

They lowered the body down, and then my poor friend was lowered down, as I had heard before, with a bottle of water and small loaves of bread. Then the large stone was placed back over the mine opening, and my friend was left with his deceased wife.

From then on, I did nothing but guard my wife. If she suffered from even a minor illness, I was filled with terror. Eventually, my terror came true, and she died from an illness.

Securities: Government Bonds Hovered and Strengthened; The 96 Series Uniquely Fell Due to Rumors of Old Notes Being Universally Accepted 210

Yesterday at the Chinese Securities Exchange, prices hovered and strengthened, with no major fluctuations. Although the number of margin accounts was large, both long and short positions were holding steady as before. There were only two days left in this month's futures, and the market showed no signs of infighting. Swap transactions were also not lively. The dull situation was still unable to be broken. The rumors regarding the 96 series of government bonds had not subsided. It was said that old notes could be universally accepted like new notes. Upon investigation, the total number of old notes that had lost their validity and had not been exchanged for new notes was less than 10 million, which could not be circulated in the market. Their black market price was mostly only around four yuan. At this time, it suddenly jumped to the same price as the market price listed on the market, more than one and a half times higher than the original value. As a result, the spot market was crowded, and there was a sudden outflow, and the market price showed signs of collapse. What was rumored like this was probably not true. However, according to common sense, since consolidation was impossible, there was no reason why old notes would suddenly receive preferential treatment alone. Yesterday's progress was stable and firm, with nothing much to be said in terms of honor or disgrace. The morning was still uncertain, and the afternoon was relatively firm. There were very few transactions by large investors, but the newly listed No. 72 was quite popular. The 96 series of government bonds, Nos. 47, 48, and 53, etc., were sold very actively, while No. 11 was already covering short positions. The situation was chaotic and more ominous than auspicious. According to the results of the market prices, except for the 96 series, which fell by five cents to two and a half cents, the rest consistently rose by five cents to two and a half cents. The total transaction volume was 11,142,500 yuan, of which the 96 series accounted for 4,585,000 yuan. Cotton Yarn: Auction and Selling Activities 211

The yarn market is lackluster and showing signs of softening. Most people have low expectations for the yarn auctions, and there are many sellers. However, according to some sources, although new goods are being delivered this month, certain parties are still buying as usual, so prices remain high. Da Kee has also purchased over three thousand bales.

Golden Rooster Slightly Softens

The opening of the spot yarn market continued the good performance of this month. However, distant months mostly tended towards short selling, and the market felt looser. General short sellers argued that spot yarn sales were weak and that Japanese yarn was being sold competitively everywhere, predicting that the future yarn market would be hit hard. Everyone sold off, but Da Kee heavily covered their shorts, buying over one thousand bales.
