Women's Corner

Women's Suicide 224

— Zi Jiu

The bright spring scenery is both tempting and annoying. Leisurely people can certainly take advantage of this beautiful weather to travel and dance all day and night, adding some festive scenery to this bright spring scenery. However, in this harmonious atmosphere, there are many unharmonious tunes that can be seen everywhere in the texts that convey messages. Opening the newspaper every day, I feel that the word "kill" is particularly active in the news after the spring, with a scene of murderous aura rushing to the sky. Now, let's put aside the various "being killed" events and focus on studying suicide.

On the 11th of this month, the Zhonghua Daily published a statistic of the number of suicides in major cities across the country in March. (See the suicide statistics table below) Two characteristics can be found from that statistics table. First: the number of suicides in metropolitan cities such as Shanghai, Guangzhou, and Hangzhou is more men than women! Conversely. In more remote cities. Such as Kunming. Kaifeng. Wuchang, etc. there are more women than men. Second: the reasons for suicide, for women, are mostly family disputes, with a total of 308 people in March, accounting for the largest number. Men are mostly due to livelihood difficulties.

The above two characteristics are linked. The reason for this, when analyzed in detail, is mostly as follows: In more remote cities, feudal forces must still be stronger than in metropolitan cities. The large family system still exists. Old and young live together. New and old mix. Here, there are inevitable conflicts in ideology, disharmony in life, and economic conflicts of interest, coupled with the teachings of the three obediences and four virtues. It is still the natural law of the head of the family and the neighbors. These can make a weak person—an oppressed person—take the road to death. In recent years, the countryside has fallen into bankruptcy: remote cities are also on the verge of decline. Nineteen out of ten men leave home, abandon their wives, and rush to other trading ports. In this annoying spring scenery, the young women in the family may be amorous, and the young widows may occasionally reveal spring feelings, which are also common in the nature of things. However, feudal society firmly locks women with the chains of chastity. If there is any damage to this chain, they will inevitably suffer the stigma of being immoral. They can neither settle under the chains nor be traitors under the feudal forces—anti-feudal traitors. The only way to end it is through suicide. Three wives and four concubines living together in one family was not a big deal in the old society. In this struggle for favor and the husband, the defeated have no way to survive, so they can only die. Early marriage has become a habit, and girls over thirty who have not yet had good news are already qualified to be old maids. If they cannot be independent, they will surely suffer double misery! Sexual misery and life misery. Sexual repression often leads to "hysteria or nervous disorders, and the above-mentioned diseases are the root cause of family disputes.

In addition, among the reasons for suicide in this statistics table, the two items of lack of freedom in marriage and unrequited love are also more women than men, so on the surface, women's suicides mostly die in the family and die in love. It seems that women's minds are particularly narrow, and only small family disputes will lead to suicide. It seems that women are particularly amorous, and they do not hesitate to sacrifice their lives for love. In fact, women in feudal society, her world is only the family, and the family is her prison. She commits crimes in prison. If she does not commit suicide, she can only escape from this prison, but this is something that only the extremely strong can do. As for ordinary new women, they mostly go into the dead end of "love supremacy." Love is her only life. If she fails, she can only die to end it. The plot of this kind of tragedy of dying in the family and dying in love is certainly very complicated, but in the final analysis, it is nothing more than feudal forces and economic problems. There are not many men who die in family disputes and love, due to the former's tolerance. Therefore, only economic problems make men commit suicide.

As for the major cities, the number of women who commit suicide is less than that of men. The reason is that the trading ports have at least been slightly washed by capitalism, and the feudal forces have become relatively weak. Therefore, as long as the economic situation of women in the upper and middle classes is not a problem, social interaction is relatively free. However, women trapped by the economy still do not enjoy that kind of welfare. Therefore, the number of suicides among women in Shanghai, Guangzhou, Beijing, and other places is relatively less than that of men. But the number is still not in the minority.

In short, feudal forces are eating people, and a society covered in a thin veil of capitalism is also eating people, but feudal forces eat more women than men!

Women's Issues Lecture

Lecture 5: Women in Medieval Feudal Society Section 1: The Feudal System and the Clan System 225

— Jun Hui

To correctly understand the status of women in medieval (4th-15th century) feudal society, we must first understand the economic production relations and social systems of this society, especially the clan system.

First, we need to know how the ancient slave labor system mentioned in the previous lecture transformed into the feudal serfdom system, and how this transformation affected women.

The ancient society that created a solemn and brilliant civilization, with the highly developed Roman Empire as its final stage, finally collapsed in the fourth and fifth centuries AD. The main reasons were:

First, the production technology of slave labor was limited by the private property system and could not develop.

Second, under the oppression of slave labor production, free farmers and handicraftsmen were on the verge of bankruptcy.

Third, under unlimited exploitation, the mortality rate of slaves increased sharply, the birth rate decreased sharply, the price of slaves soared, and the source of slaves dried up.

Fourth, slave rebellions arose one after another, and the decadent free people were unable to maintain social order.

In this way, the slave system, which had once promoted the development of social productive forces, became a shackle hindering the development of productive forces. Therefore, the new social form that broke its shackles from the womb of this old society and hatched out was the medieval feudal serfdom society.

Serfdom society and slave society are essentially the same thing. Serfs were composed of freed slaves, bankrupt free people, and people from conquered regions. The main producer in feudal society differed from slaves in that slaves were directly subordinate to the master, while serfs were subordinate to the land owned by the master. Therefore, the serf system can be said to be a mitigated slave system! It can also be said to be an intermediate form between slaves and modern laborers.

The characteristic of the feudal social system is that conquered land was entirely owned by the great lords (kings), who then divided the land outside their directly governed areas into fiefdoms or territories and distributed them to lesser lords (vassals). Lesser lords then divided them among their retainers (staff), and the retainers further divided them among the serfs. In this way, there was an absolute relationship of command between great lords, lesser lords, retainers, and serfs, with military service as the main obligation. Serfs were engaged in agriculture, and in their total production, they contributed everything except the minimum necessary living materials to the lord, and had no right to move or choose a profession. They were bought and sold together with the land, and losing the land meant losing their basis for survival. At that time, handicrafts and commerce were not very developed, and a closed natural economy dominated the entire social life.

The clan system built on this economic foundation was also characterized by absolute subordination. The relationship of wife to husband, children to parents, and family to the patriarch was the same as the relationship of serf to lord, all with absolute obedience. This relationship was rationalized and justified by institutions such as law, religion, morality, and education!

In the ancient slave labor era, women had already been driven into the home. In the feudal era, they were even more bound by various systems, completely losing their status as "people." For example, "Three Obediences and Four Virtues, Seven Reasons for Divorce" were typical moral codes that restricted women in general feudal countries. In particular, the feudal clan system placed women under the absolute control of male authority, making them lifelong slaves of men. As the saying goes, "Marry a chicken, follow a chicken; marry a dog, follow a dog," which is the most profound expression of the status and suffering of women in feudal society!

In the era of closed natural economy, the economic tasks of the family were very important. It was a cell of the social organism of the feudal state, a unit of economic production. The unity and consolidation of a family's property was a major condition for maintaining the feudal state. Therefore, in feudal society, the authority of the patriarch was particularly strengthened, and the entire family unconditionally obeyed the orders of the patriarch.

Feudal law, in order to preserve the family property passed down from generation to generation, adopted the system of primogeniture. According to this system, the inheritance after the death of the patriarch could be inherited by the patriarch's eldest son. Therefore, the patriarch attached great importance to his eldest son. If the mistress did not give birth to a son, she would not only be subjected to abuse by the family, but also to discrimination by society. In some parts of Germany, the autonomous legal system stipulated that men who could not have sons should allow their wives to have relations with neighbors in order to have successors. The practice of wife-renting and concubinage in China was also mostly justified by the lack of sons.

The feudal state regarded the family as an independent entity, and made each individual absolutely subordinate to the family, and prevented all changes in the family. There were two reasons for this: first, to make the family the most effective economic cell for production, and second, to make the family reproduce and promote population growth.

The family forms of the feudal era cannot naturally be observed with a unified concept! In this society, there were different class groups, such as lords, knights, handicraftsmen, merchants, and farmers, each with different social lives, and their family relationships also differed. I would like, in this lecture, to observe the status of women in feudal society from the economic activities of each class, their social lives, and even their family and marriage forms.

The Painful Life of Rural Women in Jiangbei 226

— Fang

The lives of women in the counties of Jiangbei, if not for the continuous natural and man-made disasters, are usually quite bearable. However, in recent years, they have been living a hellish life that is unimaginable to women of the educated class!

Some rural women near the county seat, unable to withstand the oppression of this hellish life, run to the city to hire themselves out and live the life of slaves. The rural women in the Huai, Xu, Hai, and Yang areas mostly live in thatched houses with insufficient sunlight, dampness, and narrowness. The windows are also very small, and the furnishings of the house are very simple. If they are a little poorer, this thatched house serves many purposes. The stove and cooking utensils are piled in a corner of this thatched hut. Whenever cooking, black smoke fills the whole area like a thick fog, making it impossible to distinguish people's faces. Because the things burned in the countryside are mostly leaves, rice straw, wheat stalks, and bean stalks, which turn to ashes as soon as they catch fire. Cooking a meal requires burning a lot, and because the stove mouth must simultaneously emit smoke and accommodate those non-fire-resistant materials, cooking a meal almost suffocates people. In summer, it is even more unbearably hot, which is what they often say: "Entering in dry clothes, and coming out in wet clothes." From this, one can see the degree of heat. Sometimes, the things used for burning are piled up next to the stove. Behind the door, there is sometimes a chicken coop, which is specially prepared for the chickens to roost. Under the coop, there are piles of chicken droppings. Whenever it is cloudy and rainy, a strange smell wafts, making it difficult to breathe. Because they are used to it, they don't feel any pain. However, there are also chicken coops specially built in the courtyard for the chickens. In this small thatched house, besides their beds, some miscellaneous grains are also piled in a corner. When it rains, some firewood is also brought into the house. At this time, there is simply no place to stand in the house. How can one talk about cleanliness and hygiene? In the eyes of the villagers, everything that is waste is very precious. For example, the ashes from under the stove, the dirty water for washing pots and bowls, and excrement, etc., are all specially stored in a pit dug in the yard in preparation for spreading them on the fields next spring. Therefore, in summer, the air is full of foul odors, and it becomes the source of all infectious diseases. The breeding of mosquitoes is particularly severe. Malaria is particularly prevalent in Jiangbei. I think this is one of the reasons.

As for their sleep time, there is no fixed time. During the busy farming season, they may not sleep all night, or they may go to bed at midnight and get up at three or four in the morning the next day. Every year in April and May of the lunar calendar, it is the wheat harvesting season. Almost at three o'clock in the morning, they are busy going to the fields to work, and they don't drag their tired bodies back until late at night. If they have small children, they leave them at home without anyone to take care of them. When they are thirsty and hungry, they pick up whatever they can eat, and even dirty water becomes a very important food or drink for them. Some are busy boiling water and cooking, or carrying water to the fields for irrigation. They are really busy non-stop.

After harvesting the wheat, they can get some free time. At this time, they also use this free time to lead young girls to weave straw hat braids, handbags, baskets, and other utensils from wheat stalks and sell them in the city, in order to exchange a few coins to subsidize their families or as their own private savings, or use these coins to buy some new decorations. They are the most capable of using free time. No matter how painful it is, they find work to do as soon as they have a little time. After weaving straw hat braids, they are busy dismantling and washing old cotton clothes or quilts, or rushing to make shoes and socks for their husbands and children to use in the winter.

After all the crops are harvested, they are busy ginning cotton, spinning yarn, and weaving cloth to make clothes. So, if you go to the countryside in the counties of Jiangbei in winter, you will often hear the "Hmm! Hmm! Hmm!" sound of cotton fluffing, the "Buzz! Buzz! Buzz!" sound of spinning yarn, and the "Clatter! Clatter! Clatter!" sound of shuttles weaving back and forth late at night. Their diligence can be imagined from this!

As for the lamps they use for lighting, they are almost still the bean oil lamps or cottonseed oil lamps used in the 18th century. Occasionally kerosene lamps are used, but that is always a minority. Even if they use kerosene lamps, it is rare to see those with glass lamp shades. The diet is also very simple. They rarely have the opportunity to eat meat all year round. They mostly eat vegetables and coarse rice. After the new wheat is harvested, they have a little chance to eat some coarse wheat flour and some wild vegetables. Because they are reluctant to eat the vegetables in their gardens, they pick them to towns to exchange for grain to survive. As for some seasonings commonly used in our cities, such as oil, salt, sauce, and vinegar, they regard them as very precious. When seasoning dishes with sesame oil, they use a chopstick with a small coin with a hole tied to one end to dip into the oil jar and drip it into the dish. When eating normally, they almost always mash some garlic and chili peppers, or green onions, with some cold water, and that is enough to complete their meal. They rarely see meat, except during festive occasions, funerals, or New Year's celebrations, even the elderly are no exception. The water they usually drink is mostly plain boiled water. Occasionally, they soak some bamboo leaves or locust leaves in the water to change the color of the plain water. When they are busy, they drink some cold water to quench their thirst.

If you want to know whether a woman in Jiangbei's Xu, Huai, and Hai areas is a virtuous wife and good mother, it is easy to identify. You just need to look at their hair to see if it is combed into a bun, or if they have a very long braid. This is because the custom in the villages of Jiangbei's counties is that all married young women wear a bun at the back of their heads. Unmarried girls keep a very long braid behind their backs. Sometimes they cover their heads with a piece of blue cloth or a towel to avoid sunlight or dirt. They rarely wear flowers or hairpins on ordinary days, unless they are getting married or celebrating the New Year. Now the custom of foot-binding in Jiangbei is no longer very prevalent, and there are foot-releasing committees organized to prohibit foot-binding. If there are intentional violations, they will be punished by being paraded through the streets barefoot. This method is quite effective.

The rural women of Jiangbei pass by in such a constant stream of pain.

Short News 227

Throughout this magazine year, we have seen newspapers filled with magazine advertisements, and bookstores filled with sample copies of various magazines. The magazine year is indeed worthy of its name, but among the piles of magazines in this magazine year, there are very few women's publications with substantial content that truly benefit women. Recently, it has been heard that a group of female writers in Shanghai, in view of the needs of the times, will publish a monthly magazine entitled "Women's Life." The content will focus on the theory and practical issues of the modern women's movement, the living conditions of women at home and abroad, and various common sense lectures, striving to be suitable for the general public of women to read. The publisher will be "Shanghai Magazine Company," it is said.

Shanghai Local Buddhist Publication Amateur Weekly

Amateur Musings

Principles and Their Applicability 228

— Zhang Jian

When we study problems, think, and even perceive phenomena, we cannot but have a standard to restrain and guide our thinking, so that our thinking can follow a certain path to compare and deduce other phenomena, and reach a thorough understanding of them. This standard comes from human history, the current society, or from the knowledge developed by the individual's continuous experience, becoming a more fundamental theoretical formula. This theoretical formula is usually called a principle.

People have no definite views on the applicability of such principles. Scholars who specialize in deductive reasoning regard principles as the only important thing, believing that as long as one starts from an established principle, anything can be deduced from it. All cosmic, social, and moral laws have a fundamental principle that is constant and unchanging, and subsequent developments are merely the manifestation of this fundamental principle in real things, becoming real forms. For example, things like truth, goodness, and beauty are pre-existing principles that transcend time and space. Truthful, good, and beautiful things are the same for humans today and humans in ancient times, on Earth and on other planets. Untruthful, ungood, and unbeautiful things cannot be regarded as truthful, good, and beautiful; nor can something be truthful, good, and beautiful at this time and space and not be so at another time and space. To understand things, we only need to obtain these fundamental and eternal principles, and we can use them to deduce everything, and we can completely guarantee that it is correct.

Scholars who specialize in inductive promotion, especially researchers who take the experience of real phenomena as the realm, generally despise principles. They believe that new things can only exist in new phenomena. Therefore, to obtain new knowledge, it is only possible to actually experience new single phenomena one by one. Because before experiencing them, one does not even know the new phenomena themselves, so how can one have a knowledge of them? Using known principles to deduce phenomena, no matter how you deduce them, you can only limit yourself to revolving around the principles themselves and cannot deduce new knowledge. Therefore, principles are unnecessary in research.

To understand whether principles are needed in research and the extent to which principles are applicable, we must first understand the relationship between things and the historical process of human knowledge, two important issues. In terms of the things in the universe, every thing, even the most special thing, is both individual and belongs to the whole, having both unique special qualities and the same kind of qualities as other things within certain limits. Therefore, there are laws that match itself, both its own special laws and its general laws. If the principle we obtain is the general law of the kind mentioned here, then it is obvious that this principle will be a range that cannot be surpassed by any single thing belonging to this general and kind. Since this is the case, then even if those single things have not yet entered our range of experience, this principle can still match it, and it is not absolutely impossible to deduce from this principle beyond the known limits, trying to obtain new things there. Moreover, our research and understanding absolutely cannot recognize the outside world without basing anything on any principle. For example, if we want to recognize that a horse is a mammal, we must at least base it on the initial principle that it feeds its young with milk to recognize that it is also a mammal, although this concept of a mammal is still induced from many facts of feeding its offspring with milk. The long-term accumulation of human knowledge and the gradual storage of experience, regardless of whether it is absolutely correct, is the principle that guides our understanding and research. If we say that our research does not need principles at all, then is historical knowledge not completely useless? However, in fact, if we leave it, it will not be easy for us to study everything.

However, the laws existing in objective things, even if we don't care whether they themselves are changing (in fact, they themselves also change with the change of things), are subject to various limitations in terms of human understanding of them, especially the stage of historical development and the limitations of social conditions. Therefore, the perfection of human knowledge cannot be completed at once, and must even be completed in infinite progress. Therefore, principles cannot become absolutely correct and unchanging things. If we blindly believe in principles and do not correspond and verify principles with constantly moving real phenomena, then these principles will lose their effect under the condition of no progress and cannot be used as tools to guide us in understanding things. Therefore, principles must be changed and can be modified. But what should we use to modify it? And what can make it change? This depends on the observation of new phenomena and the result of the experience of real phenomena. Therefore, principles also need the observation and experience of facts to supplement them.

However, we are not saying here that principles of any nature are necessary for our research. For a principle to have the necessity of guiding research, it must first be the result of abstraction from objective facts, the result of research, rather than the result of taking the principle itself as the starting point of research and re-producing it from it. Any product of a void and illusory principle and its reproduction, because it cannot adapt to nature and history, is therefore not correct. If it wants nature and society to adapt to it, it will inevitably be rejected by them, and we will not be able to use it as the starting point of research. On the contrary, if it is a principle formed by reality, then this principle is the result of research from the beginning of its birth. Therefore, if it is used as an indicator of research, this is not taking the principle as the starting point of research, but using the laws of things that have first broken into the human cognitive circle to deduce and seek other unknown things that are governed by the objective general and its laws. Such principles are not only necessary in research, but also have the ability to guide us to recognize new things.

In short, the principle that can guide our understanding and research is a product of experience; but once it is produced, it will turn around and dominate us to re-experience, and this re-experience will in turn constantly enrich and improve the principle, pushing it to a higher stage of development. In this way, true principles are not only not absolutely unchanging, but they also need to make themselves more correct and more scientific in the process of evolution, and play an important role in understanding and research. Those who do not want principles and those who adhere to dead principles will not be able to study phenomena and recognize the dynamic outside world.

Timely Articles

Another Spring of Singing Birds and Falling Flowers 229

— Jun Hui

"Spring sleep unaware of dawn, everywhere one hears singing birds. Last night the sounds of wind and rain, who knows how many flowers have fallen?" Dwelling on the enchanting Xuanwu Lake in this intoxicating spring, it's easy to recall this sorrowful verse. Yet, I don't love it; rather, I feel it's a eulogy to "spring's decline" and "falling flowers." I adore the youth of spring and don't want it to age. I cherish fresh blossoms and don't want them to wither. Therefore, I most dread reciting this "eulogy."

I've been living on the lake for almost two months. Though I hear fewer "singing birds," I witnessed a "falling of flowers" once. About a dozen days ago, the tender pink cherry blossoms adorned Xuanwu Lake beautifully, especially the young cherry trees outside my window, whose flowers bloomed even more vibrantly and brightly. Each time I opened the window, I felt they were smiling at me. That smile, oh, it was more intoxicating than the smile of a maiden. At that time, my ideal was: lovely flowers, I want to protect you and ensure your lasting existence, not allowing anyone to ravage you. But that night, I first heard the wind rattling the window frames, then the rain drumming against the window paper. My ardent heart immediately trembled, worried that the pure, delicate blossoms would be sullied and assailed by the wind and rain. Yet, I consoled myself: though the wind and rain are brutal, perhaps they won't harm innocent flowers; though the flowers are delicate, they also possess a stubborn spirit and youthful vigor, perhaps they can resist. So, I peacefully closed my eyes, seeking solace in dreams!

The next morning, the golden sunlight had filled the entire room before I reluctantly jumped out of bed. With no time for washing and grooming, I quickly pushed open the window frames. As I opened the window, I fully expected the flowers, after their baptism, to be even more exquisite than before. But as my eyes swept over the garden, what met my gaze was not the usual "smile," but a sorrowful, sickly appearance. Though I was plunged into an abyss of shock, I also doubted the accuracy of my own eyes. So, I quickly leaped out the window and rushed to the cherry trees, inspecting every tree and branch in detail. Many flowers had indeed fallen, leaving only sparse, diseased remnants on the branches! Then, surveying the ground, I discovered countless petals shedding tears at me. There were also many corpses, already buried in the mud, a deeply saddening sight. At this moment, I deeply felt ashamed: one like me, who loves flowers but cannot protect their lives, is ultimately not a true flower lover. Though I once styled myself as a protector of flowers, I ultimately failed to fulfill the responsibility of protection!

Nevertheless, I still love flowers. On one hand, I grieved the tragic death of the flowers outside my window, and on the other hand, I worried about the fate of flowers elsewhere. So, with a bitter heart, I reluctantly made a tour of the entire lake. But everywhere I went in the cherry orchards, I saw only bare, broken branches, and those scattered petals, lying on the ground, panting and sighing! Finally, I climbed to the top of a high mound, moving my eyes to survey the entire lake: what met my gaze was not the usual exquisite beauty, but a bleak, sorrowful countenance. Facing this desolate, desolate scene, I could no longer bear the bitterness in my heart. I wanted to collect the flower corpses for a solemn burial, but that would be too sentimental. At the same time, I also thought that the exposure of the flower corpses would only serve to display the brutality of the wind and rain: its one night of unbridled power had cut short countless young lives!

As I walked home, listening to the "yang wu" (crows) incessantly wailing, each cry seemed to spread the bad news of the flowers. At this moment, I couldn't restrain the anger in my heart and couldn't help but secretly scold:

"You glib-tongued little crow, who asked you to spread this ill tidings? Where were you hiding when the storm raged last night? Take away your false compassion!"

Now, the peach and plum blossoms are in full bloom again. The peach blossoms are bright red, the plum blossoms are pure white, and this combination of red and white colors makes the entire Xuanwu Lake even more beautiful and radiant. Every day, I wander among these clusters of flowers, sometimes acting as a flower protector, and at the same time, enjoying the fragrance of the flowers and admiring their delicate beauty. How happy is my state of mind!

But facing these fresh and lively flowers, I also think of the fallen petals. Weren't the cherry blossoms just as fresh and lively before? But after one night of wind and rain, they became fragmented corpses. The peach and plum blossoms of today are so fresh and lively, but who knows if tomorrow they will not change into another form? If another storm comes tonight, what will be the outcome?

The wind and rain have no feelings. Their brutality knows no end. If they are pleased to unleash their unbridled power, the fragile flowers will be their victims! The cherry blossoms of the past were vividly sacrificed under their unbridled power. Can the peach and plum blossoms of today hope for their mercy? My ardent heart is truly worried for them! But while I worry for them, I am also annoyed by their excessive delicacy: they only know how to compete with their own kind in beauty and charm, without thinking of how to resist external violence. They only have beautiful appearances, without strong lives; only the inertia of surrender, without the spirit of struggle.

However, I still love them. But the single word "love" cannot transcend their wretched fate. Now it is late spring, and their lives have just reached their peak. If they are once ravaged by wind and rain, then the entire flower kingdom will be exterminated, and spring will also be declared shattered at the same time! Therefore, recently, whenever I hear the "crow's cry" in the early morning, I think that the bad news of the flowers has arrived. So, I hurriedly push open the window to see if it was windy and rainy last night. Because my experience is: the reason why crows cry is not only to spread the bad news of "falling flowers," but also to report that a storm is about to arrive. Therefore, I most fear hearing the crow's cry, and also fear remembering the "eulogy"-like verse—"Spring sleep unaware of dawn, everywhere one hears singing birds. Last night the sounds of wind and rain, who knows how many flowers have fallen?"

Various Industry Investigations

New Village Enterprise 230

— Chao

Since the Industrial Revolution, cities have expanded rapidly, and the countryside has become increasingly barren. However, urban life is a purely mechanical and unnatural one. Therefore, a major issue in society now is how to make cities possess the joys of the countryside and how to make the countryside also have the benefits of the city. To achieve this goal, it is necessary to "ruralize cities" and "urbanize the countryside," and the new village system has arisen in response to this need.

England's industrial and commercial development was the earliest in the world, so the need to transform English cities is also the most urgent. The establishment of new villages first originated in England. Before the European War, the number of new villages in England had reached more than fifty. Recently, countries in Continental Europe have also followed suit and established new village organizations. For example, Germany has established an association in Berlin and branches in various places. France has also established its headquarters in Paris, and its branches have been extended to Belgium, the Netherlands, and other countries. The best results in operating new villages in Continental Europe have been achieved by the Krupp ironworks' workers' new village in Essen, Prussia. The second best is the new village created by Pullman, the owner of the Pullman Car Company factory in America. Its architectural structure focuses on cleanliness, and every residence must be attached to a garden, so that flowers and trees are in bloom in all seasons, making it the most beautiful new village.

The new village movement now has a tendency to sweep the world. The construction of new villages in Continental Europe, as well as North and South America, India, Japan, and other countries, is increasing daily. Looking back at our country, although the development of industry and commerce is still slow, the evils of cities are already very obvious. Today, the primary goal of our government is to find ways to avoid the evils of cities, so the construction of new villages is extremely urgent. After the May Fourth Movement, although Mr. Zhou Zuoren made great efforts to promote it, giving the people of the country an impression of the new village movement, unfortunately, no true new village has yet appeared.

Since the China New Village Construction Society and the Xinhua Bank separately established new villages, people across the country have paid close attention. It is understood that the first new village established by the society is called "Rose Garden New Village," which covers an area of 100 acres in Xijiatang on the Shanghai-Minhang Road, and is adjacent to the Shanghai Middle School affiliated with Jiangsu Province. Construction has already begun, and about a dozen residences will soon be completed. Its transportation with the Shanghai Concession is via the Shanghai-Minhang Road, and the village also has its own buses that travel between the village and the Bund on Nanjing Road. In addition to transportation, other public facilities for residents, such as running water, electricity, telephone, postal service, markets, etc., are all available. In terms of public services, such as education, there is a complete elementary school with a kindergarten, and plans are underway to establish a library and sports field. In terms of health, a health center (equivalent to a small-scale hospital) is specially set up to plan public health services. In addition, the architectural plan of the village is originally a garden-style village, with dozens of acres of open space planted with trees and flowers, and a designer is specially hired to arrange everything. A park is also set up in the village for residents to rest and play. In order to improve economic life, cooperative enterprises are specially advocated. On the one hand, it connects residents to launch a cooperative enterprise promotion association, and on the other hand, it establishes a household assistance group to promote household cooperation. A family craft room is also set up to create service opportunities for women in the village, inviting housewives in the village who are proficient in family crafts to be responsible for guiding silkworm rearing, silk reeling, bee keeping and honey brewing, as well as weaving, embroidery, knotting, sewing, and other crafts to enrich the meaning of women's lives.

The engineering design of the houses adopts a modern style on the outside; the balanced layout adopts a convex and concave overlapping style. The houses are independent, each with its own private garden. But it also attaches great importance to the scenery of the entire village, so that it becomes consistent and forms a large garden. Whether viewed from a distance or up close, there are no drawbacks of emptiness or obstruction. The internal structure of the houses is designed with comfort and practicality in mind, without being wasteful or too narrow and cramped. It is also decided to build a magnificent and splendid civic hall in the center of the village as a place for residents to hold weddings, funerals, celebrations, or public gatherings at ordinary times, hoping to encourage residents to spontaneously organize various clubs and societies, so that the entire village has a spirit of mutual assistance and cooperation. In terms of security, in addition to building a strong and dense fence of more than ten feet high around the village, a section of iron railing has been built along the Shanghai-Minhang Road. The Shanghai County Government has built a bunker about a hundred steps away from the village gate, and will set up a police station in front of the village gate to station guards on a regular basis.

Initially, the society announced the first phase of its plan, stipulating that the residences in Rose Garden New Village would be of three types: A, B, and C, and each level would be divided into three styles for residents to freely choose. The prices of the three A-level styles were set at 9,000 yuan per house, occupying one mu of land. The prices of the three B-level styles were set at 12,000 yuan, also occupying one mu of land, but with more rooms. The prices of the three C-level styles were set at 18,000 yuan, occupying two mu of land. The above prices include: (1) land price, (2) construction cost, (3) sanitation equipment, (4) private garden and ground plants, (5) public buildings in the village (including roads, auditoriums, libraries, sports fields, parks, health centers, elementary schools, kindergartens, public kitchens, new village management offices, police stations, markets, etc.) (6) public facilities in the village (including buses, electricity, telephone, running water, fire fighting equipment, etc.). Those who order houses first select the demarcated base, location, and house style. (The society also has a general site map, house drawings, and various reference tables.) They can estimate their own economic strength and adopt the method of paying in full at once or paying in installments. This method of paying in installments is actually the same as paying rent monthly for those who rent houses in Shanghai. First pay the land price and a deposit of about one-quarter of the total price, and then you can repay it monthly from two to ten years according to your own wishes. However, ordinary rent payments are indefinitely burdened permanently, while ordering a house in Rose Garden New Village allows you to set the rent payment period yourself, and you can obtain ownership of the real estate when it expires. Therefore, since the first phase of the plan was announced, dozens of people have ordered houses. Later, in order to popularize the plan among urban salaried classes and in view of the economic downturn in various industries, in order to reduce the burden on those who pay rent monthly indefinitely, the second phase of the popularization plan was announced.

The second phase of the popularization plan divides the residences into two levels: D and E. Each level is divided into two styles. The architectural forms are beautiful and solid both inside and out. You only need to pay a construction fee of 500-600 yuan in advance, and then you can pay the rent in installments annually and monthly. According to the pre-determined contract, you can obtain ownership of the real estate when the rent is paid in full upon the expiration of a certain number of years. This method is called the "subscription for construction and rental with periodic acquisition of real estate ownership in installments method." The longest period is twelve years, and the shortest is one year. D-type properties are quite similar to double-fronted Western-style residences in Shanghai, but occupy half a mu of land, and have sanitation equipment and a private garden; E-type properties are similar to single-fronted small Western-style houses in the city, but are double-fronted flat-roofed, also occupy half a mu of land, and have sanitation equipment and a private garden. It is said that there are now many people subscribing for construction and renting D and E-type houses, because the rent is less than that in the city, and the life and environment are much more comfortable and beautiful than in the city.

Recently, well-known banks in this city, such as Guohua Bank, Szehsing Savings Society, and their various branches, are all happy to act as agents for the society to handle subscription orders for residents, which further increases social belief in the advocacy of the new village movement. Moreover, the society also has extremely novel contributions to the expansion of the new village base and cooperative investment in the construction of new villages. The society has now announced a special method of cooperative investment in new village housing, wanting to put stagnant funds to safe use. They divide the investment in new village real estate into two types: (1) arbitrary investment, which does not fix a number, with 500 yuan in national currency as the minimum. Investors can estimate their own financial resources and determine the number themselves. (2) whole-house investment, which can be determined based on the type of new village residence, but one person can invest in a maximum of ten houses. This investment method adopts a resident cooperation system. Both parties are based on the spirit of concerted efforts in advance. The resident party can obtain ownership of the real estate upon the expiration of the subscription for construction and rental period, while the investor party has no worries about vacant rentals. Only after there are people who have subscribed for construction and rental housing is cooperative investment solicited, thus balancing supply and demand. You can also set the period in advance according to your own wishes. It is equivalent to exchanging cumbersome real estate for valuable bonds. At the same time, from the perspective of rescuing bankrupt rural areas, it is also the only way to develop productive enterprises with stagnant capital. The new village is a model village, which not only improves the chaotic urban living environment, but also gradually makes the countryside scientific. With the new village to disperse the accumulated wealth of the business community, to comfort the narrowness and bitterness of the city. In normal times, personnel and business conditions can be adjusted, so that there is no worry about wealth accumulating and having nowhere to use it; in the event of war or major natural disasters, because guarding and defense are customary, unity and cooperation can help each other, and the essence of the city will not be completely destroyed because it is concentrated in one place. If it were not for the many new villages—rural cities—in England during the European War and Japan during the Great Earthquake, I am afraid that the tragedy of the entire city's destruction would have already been staged.

Miscellaneous Writings

Exodus 231

— Shi Yong

This beautiful hometown is devastated. This hometown nurtured by verdant scenery, this hometown where more than two thousand people dreamed beautiful dreams, this hometown with the active traces of countless generations of ancestors, this hometown with rows of houses and beautiful pastoral gardens is devastated.

Jin Sheng looked back and thought of his own home, tears welling up in his eyes.

Zhang Lingfu, sitting at the bow of the boat, shouted violently: "Damn it, other people's boats have already passed Tangwan. You don't care about the lives of everyone on this boat!"

The boat also turned past Tangwan. The road, which used to have few pedestrians, now also had groups of people running as fast as they could.

Jin Sheng saw Uncle A Jiang, hunchbacked and carrying two heavy quilts, squeezed into the crowd, moving like a snail. This old man was being left behind by the young people. The old man's footsteps suddenly stopped, and the hunchbacked back disappeared. Jin Sheng was puzzled. Then the old man was carrying the hunchbacked back forward again, but the objects on his back seemed to have been reduced by half.

There was another woman, like Li's younger brother's woman, carrying a child on her back, and also leading a larger child in her right hand. The child was not used to running fast, crying and shouting, the shrill sound agitated the thin air, and the mother still dragged him along with difficulty.

The road was getting closer to the river bank. Jin Sheng saw that there were scattered large and small packages tied up tightly on the bank, clothes that were too heavy to carry on the long journey, and had to be abandoned.

— Wah...wah...um...

A two-year-old girl, like the clothes, was abandoned in the vegetable field, her voice hoarse, no one willing to take her with them.

— Hey, Uncle A Jiang, where are you escaping to? Why didn't your son and daughter-in-law take you with them? Jin Sheng raised his voice to ask the person on the dike.

A Jiang gasped sadly.

— Everyone is fleeing for their lives! The house was hit by a × foreigner's bomb!

— Where to?

— Where to? Go to Lujiazai to take shelter.

— Hey, hey, Uncle A Jiang, Zhang's family at the end of West Market Street... Hey, hey, Zhang Lingfu's family, is everything alright?

Zhang Lingfu made a sound like a broken gong.

— Don't mention it, don't mention it. Bombs are like bird's eggs, a dozen or so fall down at once. Hey, the end of West Market Street is okay, the worst is the city center.

After A Jiang said this, the people at the end of West Market Street showed a slight joy, but the faces of those in the city center turned pale.

— Hey, Uncle A Jiang, we, Li... Hey, on Daqian Street...

— Me, Zhang Delong... Uncle A Jiang!

— A Jiang...

Everyone was talking at once, A Jiang couldn't handle it, and just shouted loudly:

— Lin Wende was bombed to death, it was really tragic! That stone flew straight to the Chenghuang Temple square and plunged three feet deep. Lin Wende's body couldn't be found...

— Ah, it's all because of installing the damn time bell in the elementary school! Damn it, it was too high and attracted attention!

— Really, didn't you see the plane always circling on top of it?

The voices became lively up and down the embankment.

The people on the boat and the people on the shore were talking loudly. The people on the boat were also talking in lower voices with each other. The women's chatterboxes were all open.

The women thought about what other things, valuable and useful things, they hadn't taken away, and hated themselves for being confused. Ah, they hadn't taken the jewelry with them either. Thinking and talking, regret and love intertwined, and Zhang Lingfu's woman cried.

Zhang Lingfu cursed: "Damn it, you woman are the most useless. The Zhang family can be considered to be all exhausted."

The people in the same boat were attracted by this couple. Hearing this, everyone laughed. But then thinking of themselves, and the great disaster to come, they immediately gathered their laughter and were attacked by sorrow again.

The Lou River turned again.

The people in the boat could only see the group of people rising and falling on the mountain-like dike. After a while, they were all gone.

— Jin Sheng, let's find a secluded reed pond to hide in for tonight, and then figure out what to do!

— Yes, we can't leave home too far. If we're too far away, what will we live on?

The weather got a little colder, and everyone felt a little chilly. The sky was getting dark.

Jin Sheng docked the boat by the side of the bank where there was a bamboo forest. There was already a boat with the same fate parked next to it.

The boat was tied up.

The young people hadn't stretched their bones all day, so they all jumped ashore and looked towards Lou Town. Looking out, the darkness was still permeating the end of the vast wilderness.

In the vast night, it could be seen that red light was rising.

Biographies

The Pure Poet Shelley (2) 233

— Written by Japanese Tsurumi Yusuke, Translated by Zhou Leshan and Qi Junfu

When this happened, after those elders who had insulted him left, he picked up the mud-covered collection of poems from the gutter, brushed the dust off his soiled clothes, and threw himself on the green grass of the pasture by the Thams River, looking up at the towering Winzer Palace, and looking down at the mirror-like flowing water.

At this time, in his hand was a volume of Political Justice by William Godwin. Meditating on the misery and injustice of human society, he swore:

"I swear by the righteous and wise freedom: I swear not to be a subordinate of self-seekers and powerful people, and dedicate my own life to the worship of beauty."

The thoughts of youth dominate a lifetime. Shelley's life was spent fighting for this riverside oath.

Four

His grandfather was full of eccentricities, and like him, he was also not at home often. His father was a typical Englishman, an ordinary man, who only knew how to float and sink with the world. The mother, however, took a strong man as her ideal and hated her eldest son for taking books to the forest to meditate. However, the three younger sisters worshipped and caressed their brother like a god.

At the age of eighteen, he entered Oxford University.

He lived simply like a child. As a hater of meat, his pockets were always full of biscuits and bread. When walking on the road, he read books while eating with a "jia da jia da" sound. He lived without knowing day and night.

At this time, he began to write novels and essays. And he printed his work The Necessity of Atheism and displayed it in the storefront of a bookstore near the university.

The next day, he was summoned by the principal and the student supervisor, who announced:

"Expulsion!"

Also expelled was his friend Theames Jefferson Hogg. They came to London together, rented a house, and began to live. The mediocre father, seeing that his son had been expelled, felt that it was related to his own face, so he went to London to force his son to change his ways. If he did not repent, he would cut off his supplies. Shelley refused his father's wishes, so he was cut off as planned.

This was the beginning of his lifelong poverty.

Soon, Hogg listened to his father's advice, abandoned him, and in the vastness of London, he was abandoned with no money. (To be continued)

Amateur Coffee Shop

Liao Hua as Vanguard 234

— Shi Xiong

Even in my childhood, I watched a legend of the Romance of the Three Kingdoms. Because I was young then, and because so many years have passed, most of the story has faded from memory. However, for some reason, the struggle of the Shu Kingdom before its demise is still vaguely remembered.

Although Kong Ming's six expeditions to Mount Qi seemed lively and tense, with many magical feats, between the lines there was already a hint of decline, desolation, and the difficulty of the struggle. When Kong Ming passed away, the Shu Kingdom's life was also on its last breath. The Five Tiger Generals, whom readers of the novel were so familiar with, no longer appeared in the text at this time. With the Shu Kingdom lacking great generals, Liao Hua actually became the vanguard. Reading this, I often sighed in disappointment.

At that time, I did not mean to belittle Liao Hua, but I just thought, how unfortunate that the Shu Kingdom was about to perish, and talented people were being buried.

Today's world is still the same as before. A, B, C, etc., are arranged in neat ranks. When A dies, B fills A's vacancy; when B dies, C fills B's vacancy. But when B dies, there is no one to succeed C, and C may not be able to shoulder the great responsibility. Therefore, "Liao Hua as vanguard" is the only option left. Even if Liao Hua himself is well aware that he is not up to the task, he can only reluctantly do his best.

The key here is that when the Five Tiger Generals were in their prime, they did not know how to encourage the next generation of talent. Once there was a gap between generations, the overall situation would be over.

Climbing up is a matter of course in the minds of Chinese people. A lifetime of hard work is just to hope that one day they can climb to the top. At that time, society in general will reward them for their past experience and their spirit of waiting for rabbits, and naturally acknowledge them as the successor. At this time, he is often no more than a talent like Liao Hua. In China, except for periods of historical upheaval that can create a few heroes, people have never been good at identifying real talent. This is probably because "youngsters becoming famous" seems to be a threat to their older predecessors.

After all, when Liao Hua was the vanguard, the Shu Kingdom was in its final struggle.

Therefore, we should learn a lesson from this: one Liao Hua cannot stop the new elite of Jin, let alone the Five Tiger Generals, so what can they do to make Liu [Shu] last forever?

Shenbao Local Supplement Film Special

Hollywood's Shady Dealings: The Audition of Movie Actors (Part 1) 240

— Fu

In this place of Shanghai, we often see news in the newspapers about young men and women being deceived by signing up for movie schools and newly established companies in the hope of entering the film industry. In reality, such things are endless. And it's not just Shanghai that has this kind of thing. Even in Hollywood, where film companies are numerous and people should have more knowledge and experience, there is no lack of such shady dealings. We will now translate some of what we have read in American film magazines.

These people who create shady dealings use all sorts of tricks and lay out a maze, waiting for young men and women with short sight, lack of experience, and excessive enthusiasm to fall into the trap. We will now reveal various inside stories, hoping that young men and women aspiring to film can gain some experience after reading this. Wasting money is secondary; wasting time, or even drifting to another place and being unable to return, is truly a tragedy.

Let's first talk about the shady dealings of stage auditions. In Hollywood and Los Angeles, there are many theaters. Because these are all regarded as the outer warehouses or showrooms of film companies—film tycoons often come to select new talent—many men and women who want to enter the film industry but have no way in want to first try their hand on stage and gain some initial experience.

Sure enough, one day, A saw a small advertisement in the newspaper: "Musical comedy, to be staged soon. Auditions for actors, singers, dancers, etc." He followed the address published in the newspaper and found the place. The room was decorated to look very presentable. The receptionist was very attentive, knowing that the god of wealth had arrived. The manager, upon seeing him, immediately said that he was exactly the person they were looking for. The conditions were also very favorable. They told him that they were in contact with a famous movie star and were assigning him an important role.

The next day, he ran over there, and they were already selecting dancers. He counted, and there were at least seventy-five of them. Even more coincidentally, not a single one was rejected. He ignored that and went to find the manager. Their conversation was still very satisfactory. After a while, the manager came out to address everyone, about a hundred people in total. He spun a yarn, saying that so-and-so was the financial backer, how the government was assisting, because this was a patriotic endeavor. Rehearsals were scheduled to begin in two weeks.

The manager also said, "Please, everyone, do not mention this matter outside, because they do not approve of advance publicity and want to amaze people in one fell swoop after the rehearsals are complete." The auditionee was somewhat suspicious at first, wondering why they had to keep it so secret, but he seemed to have heard of the name of the big shot, and with the government's assistance, it was probably not a lost cause.

After many days, their play was about to be rehearsed. One day, they, the young men and women who had been selected, all received a notice that rehearsals would begin the next day. They all arrived on time. They were invited into the manager's office in rows. The manager, looking worried, told everyone that the musical comedy was scheduled to debut in Seattle within six weeks, but that the big shot had suddenly died. He said that his own money was almost gone. Now he was short of some maintenance funds. He wanted to sell the entire troupe, assets, etc., to someone else. But selling it to someone else and letting them make money—money that was almost guaranteed—was not as good as having their own people take over. If each of them was willing to contribute ten dollars as a share, the rehearsals could continue. After the opening, they would surely make money, a small investment with huge profits.

Many people thought what he said made sense and readily agreed, especially since ten dollars wasn't much. But ten dollars per person, a hundred people is a thousand dollars. Of course, the play never opened. The movie star mentioned was later encountered, and she had no idea about this at all. The so-called big shot either didn't exist at all, or did exist, but hadn't died.

A month later, the auditionee saw a similar advertisement in another newspaper. He was a veteran and had more experience, but he still wanted to try, hoping to encounter something real. He went to the address as usual. He found it. He walked into the manager's office. As before, they told him that he was exactly what they needed and asked him to come back tomorrow to get the script.

The next day, he went again. He was surprised to find that he wasn't the only one being given a script and told to study it. But the manager saw his suspicion, walked over, and whispered to him, "Don't worry. They're just putting on a show. The role has already been assigned to you." He also told him that the others weren't qualified enough. The manager even gave him a script, told him to read it carefully, and asked him to come back next week for the official rehearsals. When next week came, he received a notice and went as scheduled. But something was wrong.

When he got there, he saw that the room was crowded with people. He thought that a theater troupe definitely couldn't accommodate so many people. He already understood in his heart that it must be some kind of trick. Sure enough, he found out that there were six people playing each role. The manager was about to distribute the lines, which were typed. But before handing them out, he announced that these lines had been lost too many times before, and now he had to recover some of the cost of the printed paper. Not much, just two dollars and fifty cents per copy. But for a hundred people, that's two hundred and fifty dollars. Not bad for five days of pay. This was his second experience. Of course, he wasn't fooled himself. (To be continued)

Film Reviews

Review of "Song of Sorrow" 241

— Ji Han

——Jin Cheng Ying

Presenting the unemployment of intellectuals as a problem to the audience, in the current wave of unemployment panic, the seriousness of the theme of "Song of Sorrow" is indeed very worthy of attention. However, having good content but not being able to express it through film techniques is a great loss. Therefore, it cannot obtain a relatively significant social response, and people sincerely regret "Song of Sorrow."

In "Song of Sorrow," the playwright very simply tells us that in this society where there are more people than jobs, the intellectual youth are being pushed closer and closer to the starvation line. However, they have a sense of justice and would rather their children die of starvation than write an article on "coexistence and co-prosperity" that sells out national interests against their conscience. These kinds of young people are people we can often come into contact with. They have great vision, they have passionate justice, however, because they have too much conscience, they are not tolerated by the current society, and so they can only walk on the dead end of life!

This is a fairly realistic tragedy, at least it should garner sympathy from intellectuals. But we can only say that the playwright had a good concept, but did not express this concept in an image-based way. The playwright cannot hide the fact that he is not organized in the story, and is presenting it in a fragmented way before the audience. What he can do is narrate one party, then drop the other party, and sometimes use accidental opportunities to connect them, without any strict structure. The development of the two lines of Hu Ping, Wang Naidong, and Li Minghui, Wang Yin, is not intricately intertwined, and then from Li Minghui, Wang Yin, a third line of Qin Tong is separated, which makes it even more confusing.

Of course, no one will ignore the director's unfamiliar techniques. His tone for the play is so slow that it makes people feel like they are in a dream. I almost suspect that this film has not been edited. If there had been better weaving, it might have achieved better results. There are few moving scenes, and the entire play is such a "promise" to the audience that it will take two hours, which I think is unnecessary.

Looking at the director's negligence from a smaller perspective, such as Wang Yin having black hair in the same scene one moment, and white hair the next. When Wang Yin's child dies, the close-up of the low-angle shot makes the child look like a doughy adult. When Hu Ping sings about Ehuang and Nuying, the movements of the four dancing girls have nothing to do with the mood of the song, truly so-called active background!

In short, here there is no expression of a balance with sorrow, no coordination of fast and slow. Several actors such as Li Minghui, Wang Naidong, Wang Yin, Hu Ping, Qin Tong, etc., have all had quite a bit of success before, but here, apart from the individual places where some of the actors' cleverness is brought into play, they are all so ordinary because the director has no good direction and handling of them. There are a few very nice sets, but without good plays to match them, they just seem like extravagant waste. As for the dubbing, it is even more immature. Apart from the reality of the theme, in terms of technique, "Song of Sorrow" cannot become a successful tragedy.

The Story of the Confiscation of the Anti-Chinese Film in Canada 244

— Huang Zhuling

The newly established Northern Film Company in Victoria, Canada, recently released an anti-Chinese film. The film is called "Black Robe," and the first act is called "Secrets of Chinatown." The content describes the mysterious Chinese societies in the Chinese area of the city, smuggling opium, and worshiping Guanyin Bodhisattva as the center of the mysterious union, etc. The film began production last year and went to a antique store run by a Chinese named Yuan to buy Chinese clothing and decorations. Yuan also introduced some unscrupulous Chinese to act as actors for the filming. After the overseas Chinese discovered this, the Chinese Association sent representatives to negotiate with the local city government and ask them to ban it, but the film had already been completed and was shown at the Empire Theater in the city in March this year. After learning about this, our country's consulate immediately sent a letter to the city government to protest and negotiated with the film censor. After receiving the letter, the censor presented it to the Ministry of Justice to order the provincial police to go to the company and confiscate the film, thus ending the matter.

Film Novel

Living on Velvet (Part 1) 245

— Ti Yun

Produced by Warner Brothers of America, starring Ke Fu Lan Qian Si and others

It was an autumn afternoon. Countless spectators gathered at Curtis Airfield to watch the air force perform. Suddenly, a foreign aircraft, most likely a privately owned one, soared into the sky. It flew back and forth wildly among the air force planes, disrupting their formation, causing those watching below to lose color, and even throwing off the rhythm of the military band. At this moment, the radio announcer reported over the loudspeaker: "No one knows what's going on... We don't know where that aircraft came from. It's disrupting the air force formation... We don't know who's piloting it... It doesn't look like a military aircraft... This is very strange... It almost collided with Captain Ramsay's plane... The stands are in chaos..."

Sure enough, after the air force formation was disturbed by the strange aircraft, it scattered and gradually descended. The strange aircraft, as if aware of the disturbance below, also flew down. After the aircraft stopped, a young man in plain clothes jumped out. He was tall, burly, with sleek black hair and an arrogant demeanor. He got out of the plane and adjusted his tie. Many flight instructors swarmed around him, surrounding him. One of them said, "The major wants to see you. Go see him."

The young man, seemingly oblivious, muttered to himself, "Sorry for parking my plane in the middle of the airfield." As he spoke, he followed a group of officers to the major. The major asked him, "What's your name?" The young man replied, "Thorpe Park." The major asked again, "What were you doing in the sky?" Thorpe Park said, "I was also flying, flying." His fearless attitude shocked the officers standing nearby and listening intently into silence.

At this point, the major jumped up and said, "Oh, you were flying, flying. Do you know that you disrupted today's air force drill formation? Tell me quickly, what's going on?" Thorpe said nonchalantly, "I'm afraid I won't speak well if I speak too quickly. But seriously, although my flying may seem to have exceeded a considerable scope, I haven't broken any laws because there are no laws in the sky. I'm afraid you can't arrest me."

At this moment, a person suddenly rushed in. His name was Walter Blystrong. He was a friend of Thorpe Park and had rushed to rescue him upon hearing the news. He didn't necessarily know that Thorpe had committed a crime. He just knew that Thorpe had returned after a year and a half of utter silence, and that a strange aircraft had been found on the airfield. He knew it must be Thorpe Park. Walter walked in, and without greeting Thorpe, he spoke directly to the major, "My name is Walter Blystrong, a close friend of General Howard. Please leave Park's matter to me. I will ensure that he doesn't re-offend."

Thorpe Park's eyebrows twitched slightly, revealing a hint of a smile, upon hearing Walter Blystrong's words. The major said, "Of course, we don't need him to participate in our air force drills here." As he spoke, he released Thorpe Park. Thorpe then said to Walter, "Shall I go move the plane over?" Walter said, "No! Let's go out together... by car... I'll drive myself." They talked all the way, mostly Walter. He said, "You wandered around for eighteen months with no purpose, and were imprisoned in Venezuela for ten days for disturbing the peace, had two plane crashes, broke two ribs, were sued once, and now you're interrupting air force drills..." (To be continued)
